Pictures]]\n| released       = {{Film date|2017|9|5|[[Grauman's Chinese Theatre|TCL Chinese Theatre]]|2017|9|8|United States}}<!--- Premiere and countries of production per [[WP:FILMRELEASE]] --->\n| runtime        = 135 minutes<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bbfc.co.uk/releases/it-film-1|title=It|work=[[British Board of Film Classification]]|access-date=August 11, 2017}}</ref>\n| country        = United States\n| language       = English\n| budget         = $35\u201340 million<ref name=\"MendelsonForbes\" />\n| gross          = $701.8 million<ref name=\"Office\">{{cite Box Office Mojo|id=1396484|title=It (2017)|access-date=March 1, 2021}}</ref>\n}}\n\n'''''It''''' (titled onscreen as '''''It Chapter One''''') is a 2017 American [[supernatural horror film]] directed by [[Andy Muschietti]]<!--- Even through the teaser trailer were credited as Andr\u00e9s Muschietti, Andy Muschietti is credited, according to the official IT movie website and billing block on poster and home media release as well as official trailer; DO NOT CHANGE ---> and written by Chase Palmer, [[Cary Fukunaga]], and [[Gary Dauberman]]. The film was produced by [[New Line Cinema]],  [[KatzSmith Productions]], [[Lin Pictures]], and [[Vertigo Entertainment]].<ref name=New>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/stephen-kings-moves-warner-bros-706062|title=Stephen King's 'It' Moves From Warner Bros. to New Line (Exclusive)|last=Kit|first=Borys|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=May 21, 2014|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160730140142/https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/stephen-kings-moves-warner-bros-706062|archive-date=July 30, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.blumhouse.com/2017/03/28/first-poster-for-stephen-kings-it-arrives-along-with-quickie-tease-of-the-trailer/|title=First Poster For Stephen King's IT Arrives; Along With Quickie Tease Of The Trailer!|last=Galluzzo|first=Rob|work=[[Blumhouse Productions]]|date=March 28, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170401060741/http://www.blumhouse.com/2017/03/28/first-poster-for-stephen-kings-it-arrives-along-with-quickie-tease-of-the-trailer/|archive-date=April 1, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> It is the first of a two-part adaptation of the [[It (novel)|1986 novel of the same name]] by [[Stephen King]], primarily covering the first chronological half of the book. The film stars [[Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd]], [[Jaeden Martell|Jaeden Lieberher]], [[Jeremy Ray Taylor]], [[Sophia Lillis]], [[Finn Wolfhard]], [[Wyatt Oleff]], [[Chosen Jacobs]], [[Jack Dylan Grazer]], [[Nicholas Hamilton]], and [[Jackson Robert Scott]]. Set in [[Derry (Stephen King)|Derry, Maine]], the film tells the story of The Losers' Club, a group of seven outcast children who are terrorized by the [[It (character)|eponymous being which emerges from the sewer]], only to face their own personal demons in the process.<!-- DO NOT REMOVE THESE NOTES -->\n\nIt is the first film in the ''It'' film series as well as being the second adaptation following [[Tommy Lee Wallace]]'s [[It (miniseries)|1990 miniseries]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.vox.com/culture/2017/3/30/15109552/stephen-kings-it-trailer-conventional-horror|title=Stephen King's It is horror at its most unconventional. The new film's trailer is the exact opposite|last=Romano|first=Aja|work=[[Vox (website)|Vox]]|date=March 30, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170330191607/http://www.vox.com/culture/2017/3/30/15109552/stephen-kings-it-trailer-conventional-horror|archive-date=March 30, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cbr.com/stephen-king-it-rating-sequel-plans/|title=It Remake Has A Rating, Plans for a Sequel|last=Staley|first=Brandon|work=[[Comic Book Resources]]|date=February 9, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170401143822/http://www.cbr.com/stephen-king-it-rating-sequel-plans/|archive-date=April 1, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://uk.ign.com/articles/2017/03/30/it-how-the-stephen-king-remake-compares-to-the-original-tv-miniseries|title=It: How the Stephen King Remake Compares to the Original TV Miniseries|last=Schedeen|first=Jesse|work=[[IGN]]|date=February 9, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017}}</ref> Development of the theatrical film adaptation of ''It'' began in March 2009 when Warner Bros. started discussing that they would be bringing it to the big screen, with David Kajganich planned to direct, before being replaced by Cary Fukunaga in June 2012. After being dropped out as the director in May 2015, Andy Muschietti was signed on to direct the film in June 2015. He talks of drawing inspiration from [[1980s in film|1980s films]] such as ''[[The Goonies]]'' (1985), ''[[Stand by Me (film)|Stand by Me]]'' (1986) and ''[[Near Dark]]'' (1987). During the development, the film was moved to New Line Cinema division. [[Principal photography]] began in [[Toronto]] on June 27, 2016, and ended on September 21, 2016. The locations for ''It'' were in the [[Greater Toronto Area]], including [[Port Hope, Ontario|Port Hope]], [[Oshawa]], and [[Riverdale, Toronto|Riverdale]]. [[Benjamin Wallfisch]] was hired in March 2017 to composed the film's musical score.\n\n''It'' premiered in [[Los Angeles]] at the [[Grauman's Chinese Theatre|TCL Chinese Theatre]] on September 5, 2017, and was released in the United States on September 8, 2017, in 2D and [[IMAX]] formats. A critical and commercial success, the film set numerous box office records and grossed over $701&nbsp;million worldwide, becoming the [[List of highest-grossing R-rated films|third-highest-grossing R-rated film]] of all time.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://time.com/4935221/it-box-office-stephen-king/|title=It Shatters Box Office Records With Massive Opening Weekend|last=Calfas|first=Jennifer|magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]|date=September 10, 2017|access-date=October 10, 2017}}</ref> Unadjusted for inflation, it became the highest-grossing horror film of all time. It received generally positive reviews, with critics praising the performances, direction, cinematography and musical score, and many calling it one of the best Stephen King adaptations.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/it-review-roundup-1035698|title='It': What the Critics Are Saying|last=Rahman|first=Abid|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=October 10, 2017}}</ref> ''It'' also received numerous awards and nominations, earning two [[Washington D.C. Area Film Critics Association]] nominations, including Best Acting Ensemble. It was nominated for the [[Critics' Choice Movie Award for Best Sci-Fi/Horror Movie]]. The film won three [[Bogey Awards]], for pulling in more than two million German admissions in 11 days.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.screendaily.com/news/never-say-die-tops-international-box-office/5123040.article|title='Blade Runner 2049' posts $49.2m international debut (update)|last=Wyche|first=Elbert|work=[[Screen International]]|date=October 8, 2017|access-date=December 9, 2017}}</ref> In addition, the motion picture was named one of the best films of 2017 by various critics, appearing on several critics' end-of-year lists.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://metacritic.com/feature/film-critics-list-the-top-10-movies-of-2017|title=Best of 2017: Film Critic Top Ten Lists|last=Dietz|first=Jason|work=[[Metacritic]]|date=December 5, 2017|access-date=December 9, 2017}}</ref> The sequel, ''[[It Chapter Two]]'', was released on September 6, 2019, covering the remaining story from the book.\n\n==Plot==\nIn October 1988, twelve-year-old [[Bill Denbrough]] crafts a paper sailboat<!--S. S. Georgie--> for [[Georgie Denbrough|Georgie]], his six-year-old brother. Georgie sails the boat along the rainy streets of small town [[Derry (Stephen King)|Derry, Maine]], only to have it fall down a storm drain. As he attempts to retrieve it, Georgie sees a clown in the drain, who introduces himself as \"[[It (character)|Pennywise the Dancing Clown]]\". Pennywise entices Georgie to come closer, then rips his arm off and drags him into the sewer.\n\nThe following summer in June 1989, Bill and his friends [[Richie Tozier]], [[Eddie Kaspbrak]], and Stan Uris run afoul of older bullies Henry Bowers, Belch Huggins, Patrick Hockstetter, and Victor Criss. Bill, still haunted by Georgie's disappearance, calculates that his brother's body may have washed up in a marshy wasteland called the Barrens. He recruits his friends to investigate, believing Georgie may still be alive. Ben Hanscom, one of Bill's new classmates, learns that unexplained tragedies and child disappearances have plagued the town for centuries. Targeted by Bowers' gang, Ben flees into the Barrens and meets Bill's group. They find the sneaker of a missing girl named Betty Ripsom, while Patrick is killed by Pennywise while searching the sewers for Ben.\n\n[[Beverly Marsh]], a girl bullied over her rumored [[promiscuity]], also joins the group; both Bill and Ben develop feelings for her. Later, the group befriends orphan Mike Hanlon after rescuing him from Bowers. Each member of the group has encountered terrifying manifestations of the same menacing clown who attacked Georgie: a headless undead boy (Ben), a sink that spews blood only children can see (Beverly), a diseased and rotting leper (Eddie), a disturbing painting coming alive (Stan), Mike's parents burning alive (Mike), and a frightening phantom of Georgie (Bill). Now calling themselves \"The Losers Club\", they realize they are all being stalked by the same entity, which they refer to as \"It\". They determine that It appears as their individual worst fears, awakening every 27 years to feed on the children of Derry before resuming hibernation, and moves about by using the sewer lines, which all lead to an old stone well hidden under an abandoned house on Neibolt Street. After Pennywise attacks them, the group ventures to the house to confront It, only to be separated and terrorized. As Pennywise gloats to Bill about Georgie, the Losers regroup and Beverly impales Pennywise through the head, forcing the clown to retreat. The group flees the house and begins to splinter, with only Bill and Beverly resolute in fighting It.\n\nWeeks later, after Beverly confronts and incapacitates her sexually abusive father<!--You could hear him still breathing when Bill finds him-->, Pennywise abducts her. The Losers Club reassembles and returns to the abandoned house to rescue her. Bowers, who has murdered his abusive father after being driven insane by It, attacks the group; Mike fights back and pushes Bowers down the well. The Losers descend into the sewers and find It's underground lair, which contains a mountain of decayed circus props and children's belongings, around which the bodies of It's child victims float in mid-air. Beverly, now catatonic after being exposed to bright lights inside It's gaping mouth, is restored to consciousness when Ben kisses her. Bill encounters Georgie, but recognizes that he is It in disguise. As Pennywise, It takes Bill hostage, offering to spare the others and go into hibernation if they let It feed on Bill. The Losers reject this, battling with It while overcoming their various fears. It is eventually defeated and retreats deeper into the sewers, with Bill declaring that It will starve during its hibernation. After finding the remnants of Georgie's raincoat, Bill finally comes to terms with his brother's death, with his friends comforting him.\n\nAs summer ends, Beverly informs the group of a vision she had while catatonic, where she saw them fighting It again as adults. The Losers swear a blood oath that they will return to Derry as adults if It returns. After the others make their goodbyes and disperse, Beverly and Bill discuss her leaving the next day to live with her aunt in Portland. Before she leaves, Bill reveals his feelings and they kiss.\n\n==Cast==\n===Main cast===\n<!--- STOP! DO NOT CHANGE! (Exclusive)|last=Disgusting|first=Mr|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=June 2, 2016|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160706233532/https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3393163/it-actors-testing-pennywise-latest-stephen-king-adaptation|archive-date=July 6, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://movieweb.com/it-movie-cast-bill-skarsgard-pennywise/|title=Stephen King's IT Has Found Its Pennywise the Clown|last=Gallagher|first=Brian|work=[[MovieWeb]]|date=June 2, 2016|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160702165224/http://movieweb.com/it-movie-cast-bill-skarsgard-pennywise/|archive-date=July 2, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://joblo.com/movie-news/it-set-visit-tilda-swinton-could-have-been-pennywise-and-more-fun-facts-310-02|title=IT Set Visit: Tilda Swinton could have been Pennywise, and More Fun Facts!|last=Walkuski|first=Eric|work=[[JoBlo.com]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=July 27, 2017}}</ref> with Mendelsohn passing on the project, as New Line wanted him to take a sizable pay cut.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.yahoo.com/movies/stephen-kings-it-adaptation-on-indefinite-119932709092.html|title=Stephen King's IT Has Found Its Pennywise the Clown|last=Sneider|first=Jeff|work=[[Yahoo! Movies]]|date=May 26, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160817102726/https://www.yahoo.com/movies/stephen-kings-it-adaptation-on-indefinite-119932709092.html|archive-date=August 17, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On June 3, 2016, ''[[The Independent]]'' officially reported, after final negotiations took place, that Muschietti had chosen actor [[Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd]] to portray the character.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/bill-skarsgard-is-the-new-pennywise-in-stephen-king-book-adaptation-it-will-poulter-a7063071.html|title=Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd is the new Pennywise in Stephen King It adaptation|last=Stolworthy|first=Jacob|work=[[The Independent]]|date=June 3, 2016|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160623172642/http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/bill-skarsgard-is-the-new-pennywise-in-stephen-king-book-adaptation-it-will-poulter-a7063071.html|archive-date=June 23, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On portraying Pennywise, Skarsg\u00e5rd stated, \"It's such an extreme character. Inhumane, It's beyond even a sociopath, because he's not even human. He's not even a clown. I'm playing just one of the beings It creates.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.vulture.com/2016/07/take-a-look-at-the-first-pennywise-image-from-it.html#|title=Wow, the First Photo of Pennywise the Clown From It's Film Adaptation Is So Cute and Cuddly, You Guys|last=Ivie|first=Devon|work=[[Vulture (website)|Vulture]]|date=July 13, 2016|access-date=July 14, 2016|url-access=limited}}</ref> Skarsg\u00e5rd described the character further, saying, \"It truly enjoys the shape of the clown Pennywise, and enjoys the game and the hunt.\" He also commented,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.slashfilm.com/pennywise-first-look/e|title='It' First Look Teases Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd's Pennywise the Dancing Clown With New Image|last=Hall|first=Jacob|work=[[/Film]]|date=July 13, 2016|access-date=July 14, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160916020333/http://www.slashfilm.com/pennywise-first-look/e|archive-date=September 16, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> \"What's funny to this evil entity might not be funny to everyone else. But he thinks it's funny.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3398694/heres-official-pennywise/|title='It': Here's Your First Look at Pennywise!!!|last=Barkan|first=Jonathan|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=July 13, 2016|access-date=July 14, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160714150637/https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3398694/heres-official-pennywise/|archive-date=July 14, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On Pennywise's design, Skarsg\u00e5rd stated, \"It's important that we do something fresh and original for this one. It's purposely not going toward that weird, greasy look.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://uk.ign.com/articles/2016/07/13/first-look-at-pennywise-the-clown-from-stephen-kings-it-movie|title=First Look at Pennywise the Clown From Stephen King's IT Movie|last=Dornbush|first=Jonathan|work=[[IGN]]|date=July 13, 2016|access-date=July 14, 2016}}</ref> He also commented on being compared to [[Tim Curry]], stating that, \"Curry's performance was truly great, but it's important for me to do something different because of that. I'll never be able to make a Tim Curry performance as good as Tim Curry.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://denofgeek.com/uk/movies/stephen-kings-it/42160/stephen-king-s-it-first-image-of-the-new-pennywise|title=Stephen King's It: first image of the new Pennywise|last=Sokol|first=Tony|work=Den of Geek|date=July 14, 2016|access-date=July 14, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160715150133/https://denofgeek.com/uk/movies/stephen-kings-it/42160/stephen-king-s-it-first-image-of-the-new-pennywise|archive-date=July 15, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://frightfind.com/steven-kings-remake-first-look/|title=Stephen King's IT Remake \u2013 First Look|last=Beach|first=Tracy|work=FrightFind|date=July 15, 2016|access-date=July 15, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160828175232/https://frightfind.com/steven-kings-remake-first-look/|archive-date=August 28, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Skarsg\u00e5rd also elaborated on his age, stating, \"There's a childishness to the character, because he's so closely linked to the kids. The clown is the manifestation of children's imaginations, so there's something child-like about that.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.ew.com/article/2016/07/13/it-movie-pennywise-first-look|title=It movie exclusive: Pennywise the Clown seen in terrifying first look|last=Breznican|first=Anthony|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=July 13, 2016|access-date=July 14, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160714175535/http://www.ew.com/article/2016/07/13/it-movie-pennywise-first-look|archive-date=July 14, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Producer [[Dan Lin]] spoke of Skarsg\u00e5rd's physical attributes: \"His build is really interesting. He's really tall and lanky, and feels a little clown like in his movement. When he came in \u2014 we had a lot of different actors read, and when he came in he had a different spin on the character that got us really excited.\"<ref name=Stranger/> Lin concluded by comparing the character with that of [[Heath Ledger]]'s [[Joker (The Dark Knight)|Joker]], \"You've had [Ledger] doing almost a clown joker, you've seen obviously Tim Curry as a clown. We wanted someone who created a Pennywise character that would stand on its own and Bill came in and created this character that frankly freaked us out.\"<ref name=Stranger/> Muschietti spoke of Skarsg\u00e5rd's Pennywise as one not to lurk in the shadows, to which he remarked, \"Pennywise shows up, he's front and center, and he does his show. He has an act. So it's weird all the time, and every little thing implies a further threat.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://ew.com/movies/2016/12/26/it-pennywise-photo-stephen-king-thriller/|title=IT: Pennywise The anticipation of him is almost scarier than the actual Pennywise scares.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://joblo.com/horror-movies/news/it-director-andres-muschietti-talks-bill-skarsgard-s-terrifying-pennywise-293|title=IT director Andres Muschietti talks Bill Skarsgard's terrifying Pennywise|last=Sprague|first=Mike|work=[[JoBlo.com]]|date=March 13, 2017|access-date=March 14, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170313213905/https://joblo.com/horror-movies/news/it-director-andres-muschietti-talks-bill-skarsgard-s-terrifying-pennywise-293|archive-date=March 13, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On selecting Skarsg\u00e5rd to portray Pennywise, Muschietti wanted to stay true to the essence of the character, and Skarsg\u00e5rd caught his attention,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3448009/heres-bill-skarsgard-cast-pennywise/|title=Here's Why Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd Was Cast as Pennywise in 'IT'|last=Miska|first=Brad|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=July 19, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170719221957/https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3448009/heres-bill-skarsgard-cast-pennywise/|archive-date=July 19, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> \"The character has a childish and sweet demeanor, but there's something very off about him. Skarsg\u00e5rd has that balance in him. He can be sweet and cute, but he can be pretty disturbing.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.list.co.uk/article/93288-andres-muschietti-confirms-prep-date-for-it-sequel/|title=Andres Muschietti Robots|date=July 16, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017}}</ref><!-- DO NOT REMOVE THESE NOTES -->\n\n* [[Sophia Lillis]] as [[Beverly Marsh]]\n:A flame-haired tomboy who fends off an abusive father at home, while forming a strong bond with Ben.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.latimes.com/entertainment/movies/la-et-mn-it-review-20170907-story.html|title='It' delivers nightmarish visuals but misses the true horror of Stephen King's classic|last=Yamato|first=Jen|work=[[The Los Angeles Times]]|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=October 20, 2017|url-access=limited}}</ref><ref name=Beverly/> Beverly's Losership wasn't defined by the fact she was abused but by her poverty.<ref name=leader/><ref name=Club/> On the character of Marsh, Muschietti stated, \"Beverly's case is of course the worst, because it's about sexual abuse on a minor.\"<ref>{{Cite web |last=Squires |first=John |date=2017-07-14 |title=Andy Muschietti Talks Holding Nothing Back for \"R\"-rated 'IT' |url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3446886/andy-muschietti-talks-holding-nothing-back-r-rated/ |access-date=2022-10-06 |website=Bloody Disgusting! |language=en-US}}</ref> In an interview with ''[[Rolling Stone]]'', Lillis spoke of Muschietti not wanting herself and her co-stars to spend too much time with Skarsg\u00e5rd: \"We actually weren't allowed to see him until our scenes, because we wanted the horror to be real.\"<ref name=\"RollingStone\">{{cite magazine|url=http://www.rollingstone.com/movies/features/it-star-sophia-lillis-on-pennywise-more-remake-details-w491148|title=Encounter With Pennywise, Remake Details|last=T. Collins|first=Sean|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=July 18, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017}}</ref> On the character of Marsh, Lillis described her as: \"Kind of a tough person. She hides herself. She tries to hide her emotions and hide her feelings. She distances herself from everyone but once she has this friend group she doesn't want to let it go because this is the only friend group that she has and so she's a very strong character.\"{{citation needed|date=April 2021}} Working with Muschietti, Lillis and he developed Marsh as rebelling against her father, with Lillis having independence with the character, while also stating, \"We definitely talked about her mother, who was never there \u2014 she wasn't even in the movie, but we talked about background for the character.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/awards/it-sophia-lillis-stene-stealer-andy-muschietti-hair-cutting-scene-1202613806/|title='It' Scene Stealer Sophia Lillis on Creating a Rebellious Beverly With Director Andy Muschietti|last=Turchiano|first=Danielle|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=November 16, 2017|access-date=November 26, 2017}}</ref> Lillis spoke of how Beverly is someone she aspires to be, relating to her her strength, her way of facing her fears: \"When I read about her, I kind of got the sense that she was someone I could definitely look up to. I would be happy if I had any similarity to her.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.teenvogue.com/story/sophia-lillis-interview-it-movie-cutting-her-hair-bill-skarsgard|title=\"It\" Star Sophia Lillis on Cutting Her Hair and What Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd Was Really Like on Set|last=Cer\u00f3n|first=Ella|work=Teen Vogue|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=March 21, 2018}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.adolescent.net/a/sophia-lillis-it-girl-crybaby|title=Sophia Lillis is an \"It\" girl: an interview|last=Riordan|first=Remi|work=Adolescent.net|date=December 20, 2017|access-date=March 21, 2018}}</ref> On her connection with her fellow co-stars she noted that the closeness of the friendships formed allowed Lillis connect with her own character: \"I relate to Beverly \u2013 the way she deals with her emotions, and the way she was around the Losers. I felt that way around the actual actors.\"<ref name=RollingStone/>\n\n* [[Finn Wolfhard]] as [[Richie Tozier]]\n:The bespectacled best friend of Bill, whose loud mouth and foul language often get him into trouble.<ref name=leader/><ref name=Club/> Wolfhard shared the first image of the Losers Club on his [[Instagram]] account, with the photo captioned as \"The Losers Club take Toronto\", showing the cast of actors who will be playing the protagonists of the piece.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://ihorror.com/stephen-kings-first-photo-new-losers-club/|title=Stephen King's IT \u2013 First Photo of the 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> He auditioned for the part of Tozier for Fukunaga's ''It'' in 2015, before Fukunaga left,<ref>{{cite of Tozier, Muschietti stated, \"We don't know much about Richie's personality, because he's the big mouth of the group. But we suppose he's also neglected at home, and he's the clown of the band because he needs attention.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.darkhorizons.com/it-director-talks-freedom-of-an-r-rating/|title=\"IT\" Director Talks Freedom Of An R-Rating|last=Franklin|first=Garth|work=[[Dark Horizons]]|date=July 16, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017}}</ref> Of his character's changes from the novel to the film, Wolfhard stated, \"Richie's always been the same. There's some similarities to the book and there's other stuff they added because some of the stuff that we said in this movie you can't say in the '50s.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.aintitcool.com/node/78262|title=Jaeden Lieberher (Bill), Sophia Lillis (Bev) and Finn Wolfhard (Richie) talk stuttering, lack of souls and pranks in this on-set interview during the making of IT!|last=Vespe|first=Eric|work=[[Ain't It Cool News]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=June 26, 2018}}</ref> Wolfhard felt that there wasn't much research required in approaching Richie: \" You just have to read the character breakdown and it helps  a lot to see the difference between the characters in the book, and the miniseries, as well to get a raw take on it.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.fearforever.com/film/it-on-set-interviews-part-2-finn-wolfhard-jaeden-lieberher-sophia-lillis-jack-grazer-and-wyatt-oleff/|title=IT-On Set Interviews Part 2: Finn Wolfhard, Jaeden Lieberher, Sophia Lillis, Jack Dylan Grazer and Wyatt Oleff|last=Seidman|first=Amy|work=Fear Forever|date=September 5, 2017|access-date=June 26, 2018}}</ref> In an interview with ''[[GQ]]'', Wolfhard spoke of how all of The Losers bonded on set, and that the friendship has carried over: \"That friendship is for real, for sure. We hang out all the time in L.A. and wherever they are.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.gq.com/story/finn-wolfhard-it-stranger-things-interview|title=It Star Finn Wolfhard on the Scenes That Terrified Him the Most|last=Carley|first=Brennan|work=[[GQ]]|date=September 13, 2017|access-date=June 26, 2018}}</ref>\n\n* [[Wyatt Oleff]] as [[It (novel)#Characters|Stanley Uris]]\n:The [[pragmatism|pragmatic]] son of a [[rabbi]], whose [[bar mitzvah]] studies are haunted by a ghoulish woman from a painting.<ref name=leader/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nydailynews.com/entertainment/movies/star-wyatt-oleff-losers-club-battle-pennywise-article-1.3480497|title='It' star Wyatt Oleff on the Losers Club's battle with Pennywise, what apart|last=Sandwell|first=Ian|work=[[Digital Spy]]|date=September 19, 2017|access-date=October 20, 2017}}</ref> On the character of Uris, Muschietti stated, \"Long story short, there's all sorts of difficult situations, and we had the chance to tell them in a movie that faces directly those conflicts the families of the young actors were very open-minded, so we could tell the about subjects that are normally very touchy.\"<ref name=\"Despair\">{{cite web|url=https://www.dreadcentral.com/news/240616/stephen-kings-andy-muschietti-barbara-muschietti-talk-hard-r-rating/|title=Stephen King's IT: Andy Muschietti and Barbara Muschietti Talk Hard R Rating|last=Barton|first=Steve|work=[[Dread Central]]|date=July 14, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017}}</ref> Muschietti made Stanley the son of a rabbi, which is a change from the novel, to add a bit of that sense of responsibility, while to show oppression from his father, with the theme of oppression being a recurring force in the story of the adults of Derry.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/06/movies/it-andy-muschietti-interview.html|title=Andy Muschietti Narrates a Scene From 'It'|last=Murphy|first=Mekado|work=[[The New York Times]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 18, 2017}}</ref> Oleff recalled his first scene shot being a speech at his bar mitzvah: \"I had a ton of lines to memorize and they even added a whole new paragraph while we were filming. I was like, Oh boy. After a while it got a lot easier to say over and over gain {{sic}} it was, like, 10 hours filming that scene.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/movie-wyatt-oleff-is-juggling-franchises-at-14-1035822|title='It' Star Wyatt Oleff Is Already Juggling Franchises at 14|last=Couch|first=Aaron|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=October 20, 2017}}</ref> On the character of Uris, Oleff spoke by stating: \"Stanley, in the group is the last one to believe that It is actually real because he just doesn't want to. It doesn't fit within his reality until something happens. He relates to everyone, but he's the one who tries to organize everything, but he can't. It's falling apart for him and his friends come to support him.\u201d<ref name=\"Losers\">{{cite web|url=https://www.aintitcool.com/node/78258|title=IT stars Wyatt Oleff (Stanley Uris) and Jeremy Ray Taylor (Ben Hanscom) talk scary movies, hopeless romanticism, cussing and learning how to be '80s kids!|last=Vespe|first=Eric|work=[[Ain't It Cool News]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=August 30, 2017}}</ref> While Oleff stated Stanley as having [[Obsessive\u2013compulsive disorder|OCD]] remarked:<ref name=FrightFind>{{cite web|url=https://frightfind.com/meet-the-new-losers-club-behind-the-scenes-with-wyatt-oleff-of-the-it-remake/|title=Meet The New Losers' Club. Behind the Scenes with Wyatt Oleff of the IT Remake |authors=FrightFind Editor |work=FrightFind|date=September 5, 2017|access-date=October 20, 2017}}</ref> \"He tries to lay everything out in his own mind pattern kinda thing. And Pennywise comes along and just shatters everything. He's definitely the most scared.\"<ref name=FrightFind/> Uris suffers from an injury sustained at the end of Muschietti's ''It'', to which Oleff remarks \"He's been scarred, I guess you can say but Stanley is scarred mentally and physically by these marks. They're permanent, so every time he would look in the mirror he'd see it and be reminded about what happened.\"<ref name=Losers/> Oleff spoke of his research into the 1980s in which his parents helped him as \"They told me a lot about the '80s and what music. I've been listening to a lot of '80s music recently. That's helped me get into character. I made a playlist of what I think Stanley would listen to in the '80s.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://uk.ign.com/articles/2017/07/27/stephen-kings-it-how-the-new-version-of-pennywise-reaches-into-the-past-to-become-scarier-than-ever|title=Stephen King's It: How the New Version of Pennywise Reaches into the Past to Become Scarier Than Ever|last=Goldman|first=Eric|work=[[IGN]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=August 30, 2017}}</ref> Oleff also spoke of the fellowship between his co-stars and himself, where he states \"I think that translates on screen. You could see the friendship we have on and off-screen. We\u2019ve been together for so long that you can see our connection, in our characters, but also it's us connecting as humans and friends.\"<ref name=\"NerdistLosersClub\">{{cite web|url=http://nerdist.com/how-the-it-cast-relates-to-the-losers-club-journey/|title=How the IT Cast Relates to the Losers' Club Journey|last=Puchko|first=Kristy|work=[[Nerdist Industries]]|date=July 28, 2017|access-date=August 30, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180620153421/https://nerdist.com/how-the-it-cast-relates-to-the-losers-club-journey/|archive-date=June 20, 2018|url-status=dead}}</ref> Relating to sensitivity in emotions, Oleff compared himself to Uris when stating: \"Stanley tries to hide his emotions and sometimes I accidentally do that as well. So I can definitely relate to him in that way. One way to describe Stanley is like the voice of reason that no one listens to and that's also me in real life.\"{{citation needed|date=April 2021}}\n\n* [[Chosen Jacobs]] as [[It (novel)#Characters|Mike Hanlon]]\n:A sweet, softly-spoken black boy living on the outskirts of Derry on his Grandfather's farm.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.aintitcool.com/node/78260|title=Chosen Jacobs (Mike) and Jack Grazer (Eddie) talk clown spit, booty shorts and bonding while making IT!|last=Vespe|first=Eric|work=[[Ain't It Cool News]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=October 20, 2017}}</ref> On the character of Hanlon, Muschietti stated, \"Long story short, there's all sorts of difficult situations, and we had the chance to tell them in a movie that faces directly those conflicts the families of the young actors were very open-minded, so we could tell the about subjects that are normally very touchy.\"<ref name=\"Despair\"/> When describing Hanlon, Jacobs stated that although Mike's more independent in characterization, he's still an eighties character, while elaborating by stating: \"I mean he doesn't have any friends growing up, isolated, black, in the eighties, in a primarily Caucasian environment, so I think he's just got a sweetness about him.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/interviews/3426601/set-visit-report-helmer-andy-muschiettis-coming-age-killer-clown/|title=We Visited the 'IT' Set and Battled Pennywise with the Losers Club!|last=Corrigan|first=Kalyn|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=October 11, 2017}}</ref> On the characterization of Hanlon, Jacobs said: \"Finding friends that accept him for who he is means a lot to him. So he would never betray that friendship, and I feel like I'm kind of that way or at least I try to be.\"{{citation needed|date=April 2021}} Jacobs also mentioned: \"I always say this because it's so true, Mike is the best friend anyone could ask for, just because he's been so isolated and he really appreciates friendships.\"<ref name=Best>{{cite web|url=https://shadowandact.com/it-star-chosen-jacobs-interview/|title='It' star Chosen Jacobs on filming with Pennywise and who he'd want to play an older version of Mike (EXCLUSIVE)|last=Mangum|first=Trey|work=Shadow and Act|date=September 22, 2017|access-date=October 11, 2017}}</ref> while stating that he was excited to portray Hanlon as: \"I loved the depth of Mike, because he's just kind of a sweet, backbone type of guy. He's the guy you bring back to moms. I appreciated being able to play that character.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.bet.com/celebrities/news/2017/09/06/chosen-jacobs-.html|title=Chosen One: Meet The Young Star Stealing Scenes In Stephen King's 'It'|last=Cane|first=Clay|work=[[BET]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=October 11, 2017}}</ref> Jacobs felt that portraying Hanlon wasn't difficult as he just had to channel the best aspects of himself, while suggesting they have many similarities and some differences.<ref name=Best/> He brought up the element of Hanlon being one of the only African-Americans in Derry, while stating that he and the other Losers all have similar isolationism:<ref name=Isolation>{{cite magazine|url=https://ew.com/movies/2017/08/11/stephen-king-it-new-photos/|title=Stephen King's It: Derry of 1989 depicts a whole world gone wrong|last=Breznican|first=Anthony|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=August 11, 2017|access-date=October 20, 2017}}</ref> \"He grew up the outsider because of racial tension, which separated him that makes him really appreciate when someone says, \u2018Hey, I like you for who you are.\u2019\"<ref name=Isolation/> Jacobs highlighted the bond Mike shares with his Losers' Club friends while also stating:<ref name=\"NerdistLosersClub\"/> \"Pennywise is just a symbol for all the hard things that happen in life that bring people together. Of course we changed. We became more mature. Some people break out of their shells, some people retract into themselves because it's scary. This horror film is more than just horror. It's a coming-of-age movie.<ref name=\"NerdistLosersClub\"/> On the experience of shooting Muschietti's film, Jacobs spoke of it as \"my favorite summer of my 16 long years on earth\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mtv.com/news/3026463/it-movie-laugh-pennywise-the-clown/|title=One IT Star Couldn't Stop Laughing The First Time They Met Pennywise The Clownlast|work=[[MTV]]|date=July 20, 2017|access-date=July 22, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170721031309/http://www.mtv.com/news/3026463/it-movie-laugh-pennywise-the-clown/|archive-date=July 21, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\n* [[Jack Dylan Grazer]] as [[Eddie Kaspbrak]]\n:A [[hypochondriac|sickly]] boy who only feels truly well when he is with his friends.<ref name=leader/><ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://ew.com/movies/2017/07/21/stephen-king-it-losers-club-comic-con/|title=The kids from Stephen King's It explain why they're 'The Losers'|last=Breznican|first=Anthony|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=July 21, 2017|access-date=August 30, 2017|archive-date=October 31, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201031230428/https://ew.com/movies/2017/07/21/stephen-king-it-losers-club-comic-con/|url-status=dead}}</ref> On the character of Kaspbrak, Muschietti stated, \"Long story short, there's all sorts of difficult situations, and we had the chance to tell them in a movie that faces directly those conflicts the families of the young actors were very open-minded, so we could tell the about subjects that are normally very touchy.\"<ref name=\"Despair\"/> The off-screen friendships began to influence the onscreen friendships, with Grazer recalling a scene where they were able to draw on their genuine feelings for one another for a particularly emotional scene:<ref name=\"Friendships\">{{cite web|url=https://www.slashfilm.com/the-it-losers-club-interview/|title=The Losers' Club: Tales From the Young Cast of 'It'|last=Hall|first=Jacob|work=[[/Film]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=June 26, 2018}}</ref> We're lifelong friends now in reality and in the movie. We're shooting a scene now where Stanley or Wyatt is breaking down and we're all huddling around him crying and it's an amazing powerful scene. Because of the friendships, it's real.\"<ref name=Friendships/> He highlighted his enjoyment of the intense scenes he had with Skarsg\u00e5rd, stating: \"I remember one scene after he was done choking me and stuff, he goes, Jack, are you okay? And I was like, 'Yeah! That was so much fun! I love what you're doing with the character, like let's do that again.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.romper.com/p/who-plays-eddie-in-it-jack-dylan-grazer-made-the-role-his-own-2407908|title=Who Plays Eddie In 'It'? Jack Dylan Grazer Made The Role His Own|last=Walsh|first=Megan|work=Romper|date=September 19, 2017|access-date=June 26, 2018}}</ref><ref>{{cite (Exclusive) |authors=TooFab Editors |work=TooFab|date=September 14, 2017|access-date=June 26, 2018}}</ref> On his experiences with Muschietti, Grazer mentioned his usage of storyboards for scenes while also stating But to break us into character \u2013 I actually felt like I was pretty close to Eddie \u2013 we'd stick to our guns about a lot of things, we really didn't back down on our opinions.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dazeddigital.com/film-tv/article/37033/1/it-kids-stephen-king-pennywise|title=Stephen King's It: meet the (1989 film)|Batman]]'' (1989) that gave him \"insight on how he could improvise or reuse those things as references to the time period.\"<ref>{{cite (novel)#Characters|Henry Bowers]]\n:A young [[sociopath]] who leads the Bowers Gang, and terrorizes the Losers' Club.<ref>{{cite character of Bowers, Hamilton stated: \"You see a lot of characters in movies who are just bullies and just there to be the antagonist and mess with the main character. With Bowers, he has so many different layers to him, with his father being the way he is and him having to live up to that.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.heraldsun.com.au/entertainment/movies/australian-actor-nicholas-hamilton-is-becoming-a-stephen-king-expert-after-the-dark-tower-and-it/news-story/17d8bfbda696b2ba43a46a8b3c5101f8|title=Australian actor Nicholas Hamilton is becoming a Stephen King expert after The Dark Tower and It|last=Wigney|first=James|work=[[The Herald Sun]]|date=September 2, 2017|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> Hamilton prepared for the role by studying Jarred Blancard's portrayal of the character in ''[[It (miniseries)|It]]'' (1990), and in Hamilton's words: \"watched all the bits of my original character\" for research.<ref name=Bowers>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2016/film/news/nicholas-hamilton-stephen-king-it-remake-1201839699/|title=Nicholas Hamilton on Filming Stephen King's 'It' Remake|last=McClendon|first=Lamarco|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=August 17, 2016|access-date=August 20, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160819192346/https://variety.com/2016/film/news/nicholas-hamilton-stephen-king-it-remake-1201839699/|archive-date=August 19, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Blancard spoke to Hamilton, with Blancard giving him advice on how to handle some of the \"psychopathic-ness\" and general meanness of Bowers.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.fearforever.com/film/it-on-set-interviews-part-1-logan-thompson-chosen-jacobs-nicholas-hamilton-and-jake-sim/|title=IT - On Set Interviews Part 1: Logan Thompson, Chosen Jacobs, Nicholas Hamilton and Jake Sim|last=Seidman|first=Amy|work=Fear Forever|date=September 3, 2017|access-date=September 28, 2017}}</ref> Hamilton added, through the character of Bowers, that \"There's stuff that I have to do that is really creepy and the opportunity to help share my psychotic side has been really fun.\"<ref name=Bowers/> Additionally Hamilton spoke of a scene shared with Ray Taylor, wherein he had to \"terrorize the hell out of him and get right in his face.\"<ref name=Bowers/> Hamilton highlighted the generic portrayal bullying and the bully in \"in any movie\", to which he stated: \"Bowers and his gang are just so much different. There's a story, there's layers, he's vulnerable at times, he's not just the dick, so I really like that. There's definitely stuff to play around with.\"{{citation needed|date=April 2021}}\n\n* [[Jackson Robert Scott]] as [[Georgie Denbrough]]\n\n:The innocent, energetic 7-year-old brother of Bill web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/03/it-remake-teaser-trailer-pennywise-bill-skarsgard-stephen-king-1202054445/|title='It' Teaser Trailer: Pennywise Creeps Back Into Our Lives|last=Calvario|first=Liz|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=March 29, 2017|access-date=March 29, 29, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\n==Production==\nThe project was in ongoing development since 2009.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/film/2009/mar/13/stephen-king-it-film-adaptation|title=It's coming, as Hollywood plans Stephen King adaptation|last=Opie|first=David|work=[[The Guardian]]|date=March 13, 2009|access-date=October 16, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161019031106/https://www.theguardian.com/film/2009/mar/13/stephen-king-it-film-adaptation|archive-date=October 19, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.fuse.tv/2016/08/stephen-king-it-movie-complete-guide-pennywise|title=The Complete Guide to the 'It' Remake: Stephen King's Pennywise Is Back|last=Dionne|first=Zach|work=[[Fuse (TV channel)|Fuse]]|date=September 30, 2016|access-date=October 16, 2016|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161018085202/http://www.fuse.tv/2016/08/stephen-king-it-movie-complete-guide-pennywise|archive-date=October 18, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.slashfilm.com/warner-bros-remaking-stephen-kings-it/|title=Warner Bros Remaking Stephen King's It|last=Sciretta|first=Peter|work=[[/Film]]|date=March 12, 2009|access-date=October 16, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161018213742/http://www.slashfilm.com/warner-bros-remaking-stephen-kings-it/|archive-date=October 18, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> The proposed film adaptation has gone through two major phases of planning: initially with [[Cary Joji Fukunaga|Cary Fukunaga]] from 2009 to 2015, with the early contributions of screenwriter [[David Kajganich]], and with [[Andy Muschietti]], with Fukunaga remaining in some capacity due to prior screenplay contributions.<ref name=Development/><ref>{{cite web|url=https://screenrant.com/stephen-king-pet-sematary-it-remakes-schrad-66877/|title=Updates on the 'Pet Sematary' and 'It' Remakes|last=Schrader|first=Chris|work=Screen Rant|date=July 1, 2010|access-date=October 16, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161018215511/https://screenrant.com/stephen-king-pet-sematary-it-remakes-schrad-66877/|archive-date=October 18, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://screenrant.com/stephen-king-it-movies-cary-fukunaga-sandy-178091/|title=Stephen King's 'It' Getting Two-Film Adaptation by 'Jane Eyre' Director|last=Schaefer|first=Sandy|work=Screen Rant|date=June 8, 2012|access-date=October 16, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160316153624/https://screenrant.com/stephen-king-it-movies-cary-fukunaga-sandy-178091/|archive-date=March 16, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.slashfilm.com/cary-fukunaga-it/#more-312794|title=Cary Fukunaga Explains the Demise of His Unconventional 'IT' Adaptation|last=Fischer|first=Russ|work=[[/Film]]|date=September 5, 2015|access-date=October 16, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161018214854/http://www.slashfilm.com/cary-fukunaga-it/#more-312794|archive-date=October 18, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\n=== David Kajganich (2009\u20132010) ===\n{{quote box\n| align = right\n| width = 35%\n| quote = \"The thing about Stephen King's writing is that he draws his characters so well, it's hard not to imagine they're real people. So it honestly didn't occur to me to try to think of actors in those roles. Pennywise is a bit of a different story, though. His manner is so crucial to what's frightening about him, and it's too much fun to imagine all of the nuances different actors could give him. I think there are a hundred actors who could each pull off a fascinating, horrifying Pennywise, and I tried not to get too attached to any one actor in my head. I think the Pennywise in this adaptation is a less self-conscious of his own irony and surreality than was [[Tim Curry]]'s Pennywise. I think it will be harder to laugh at his antics since, under the permissiveness of an R rating, I was able to give him back a lot of his more upsetting moments from the novel, ones that could never be aired on network television.\"\n| source =David Kajganich, on the construction of Pennywise.<ref name=lilja>{{cite web|url= https://liljas-library.com/showinterview.php?id=73 |title=Interview: David Kajganich |work=Lilja's Library |date=June 29, 2010 |access-date=2021-01-30}}</ref>}}\n\nOn March 12, 2009, ''[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]'' reported that [[Warner Bros. Pictures]] would be bringing [[Stephen King]]'s novel to the big screen, with David Kajganich to adapt King's novel, while Dan Lin, [[Roy Lee]] and Doug Davison would be producing the piece.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2009/film/features/warner-bros-taps-kajganich-for-it-1118001188/|title=Warner Bros. taps Kajganich for 'It'|last=McNary|first=Dave|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=March 12, 2009|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160719080933/https://variety.com/2009/film/features/warner-bros-taps-kajganich-for-it-1118001188/|archive-date=July 19, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> When Kajganich learned of Warner Bros. plans to adapt King's novel, he went after the job.<ref name=lilja/> Knowing that Warner Bros. was committed to adapting ''It'' as a single feature film, Kajganich began to attempt to try to find a structure that would accommodate such a large number of characters in two different time periods, around 120 pages, which was one of Warner Bros. stipulations.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.slashfilm.com/screenwriter-gives-update-on-big-screen-adaptation-of-stephen-kings-it/|title=Screenwriter Gives Update on Big Screen Adaptation of Stephen King's It|last=Sciretta|first=Peter|work=[[/Film]]|date=July 1, 2010|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160524144215/http://www.slashfilm.com/screenwriter-gives-update-on-big-screen-adaptation-of-stephen-kings-it/|archive-date=May 24, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Kajganich worked with Lin, Lee, and Davison on ''[[The Invasion (film)|The Invasion]]'' (2007), and he knew they would champion good storytelling, and allow him the time to work out a solid first draft of the screenplay.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.popcrunch.com/it-movie/|title=Stephen King's \"It\" Bound For Big Screen|last=Castina|work=PopCrunch|date=July 6, 2010|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160815153332/http://www.popcrunch.com/it-movie/|archive-date=August 15, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Kajganich spoke of the remake being set in the, \"mid-1980s and in the present mirroring the twenty-odd-year gap King uses in the book and with a great deal of care and attention paid to the backstories of all the characters.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://dreadcentral.com/news/10860/exclusive-more-on-the-it-remake-rated-r/|title=Exclusive: More on the IT Remake! Rated R?|last=Barton|first=Steve|work=[[Dread Central]]|date=April 5, 2009|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160804120207/https://dreadcentral.com/news/10860/exclusive-more-on-the-it-remake-rated-r/|archive-date=August 4, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nKajganich also mentioned that Warner Bros. wished for the adaptation to be rated R which he furthered by saying, \"we can really honor the book and engage with the traumas that these characters endure.\", while Kajganich spoke of Warner Bros. wanting the adaptation as a single film.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.slashfilm.com/remake-of-stephen-kings-it-will-be-rated-r-and-set-in-the-mid-1980s/|title=Remake of Stephen King's It will be Rated-R and Set in the Mid-1980s|last=Sciretta|first=Peter|work=[[/Film]]|date=April 5, 2009|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160829002848/http://www.slashfilm.com/remake-of-stephen-kings-it-will-be-rated-r-and-set-in-the-mid-1980s/|archive-date=August 29, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On June 29, 2010, the screenplay was being re-written by Kajganich.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://dreadcentral.com/news/18143/early-details-on-the-it-remake/|title=Early Details on the IT Remake|last=Serafini|first=Matt|work=[[Dread Central]]|date=June 30, 2010|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160808233147/https://dreadcentral.com/news/18143/early-details-on-the-it-remake/|archive-date=August 8, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> He said that his dream choice for Pennywise would be [[Buster Keaton]] if he were still alive, and the Pennywise that Kajganich scripted was \"less self-conscious of his own irony and surreality.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://joblo.com/movie-news/screenwriter-david-kajganich-gives-an-update-on-stephen-kings-it|title=Screenwriter David Kajganich gives an update on Stephen King's It|last=Stephens|first=Niki|work=[[JoBlo.com]]|date=July 1, 2010|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160804190540/https://joblo.com/movie-news/screenwriter-david-kajganich-gives-an-update-on-stephen-kings-it|archive-date=August 4, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\n=== Cary Fukunaga (2012\u20132015) ===\n{{quote box\n| align = right\n| width = 35%\n| quote = \"I am in the midst of rewriting the first script now.  We're not working on the second part yet. The first script is just about the kids. It's more like ''[[The Goonies]]'' (1985) meets a horror film. We're definitely honoring the spirit of Stephen King, but the horror has to be modernized to make it relevant. That's my job, right now, on this pass. I'm working on making the horror more about suspense than visualization of any creatures. I just don't think that's scary. What could be there, and the sounds and how it interacts with things, is scarier than actual monsters.\"\n| source = \u2013 Cary Fukunaga, on the development of ''It''.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/cary-fukunaga-true-detective-interview/|title=Director Cary Fukunaga Talks TRUE DETECTIVE, Making an 8-Hour Film, Future Seasons, BEASTS OF NO NATION, Modernizing Horror with IT, and More|last=Radish|first=Christina|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=January 11, 2014|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160807054534/http://collider.com/cary-fukunaga-true-detective-interview/|archive-date=August 7, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n}} On June 7, 2012, ''[[The Hollywood Reporter]]''  had revealed that Cary Fukunaga was boarding the project as director and will co-write the script with Chase Palmer, while Roy Lee and Dan Lin are producing, as with [[Seth Grahame-Smith]] and David Katzenberg of KatzSmith Productions.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/stephen-kings-be-adapted-by-334899|title=Stephen King's 'It' to Be Adapted by Cary Fukunaga into Two Films (Exclusive)|last=Kit|first=Borys|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=June 7, 2012|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160706192550/https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/stephen-kings-be-adapted-by-334899|archive-date=July 6, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On May 21, 2014, Warner Bros. was announced to have moved the film to its [[New Line Cinema]] division, with overseer duties conducting by New Line's Walter Hamada and Dave Neustadter, along with Vice President of Production at Warner Bros., Niija Kuykendall.<ref name=New/> On December 5, 2014, in an interview with ''[[Vulture (website)|Vulture]]'', Dan Lin announced that the first film will be a [[coming-of-age]] story about the children tormented by [[It (character)|It]] and the second will skip ahead in time as those same characters band together to continue the fight as adults.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://comingsoon.net/movies/news/389569-stephen-kings-it-will-shoot-next-summer|title=Stephen King's IT Will Shoot Next Summer|last=Evry|first=Max|work=Coming Soon|date=December 5, 2014|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160303172056/https://comingsoon.net/movies/news/389569-stephen-kings-it-will-shoot-next-summer|archive-date=March 3, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Lin also stated that Fukunaga was only committed to directing the first film, though was currently closing a deal to co-write the second. Lin concluded by mentioning King, to which he remarked, \"The most important thing is that [King] gave us his blessing. We didn't want to make this unless he felt it was the right way to go, and when we sent him the script, the response that Cary got back was, 'Go with God, please! This is the version the studio should make.' So that was really gratifying.\"<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.vulture.com/2014/12/fukunaga-to-shoot-stephen-kings-it-next-summer.html |title=Cary Fukunaga Will Shoot Stephen King's It Next Summer|last=Buchanan|first=Kyle|work=[[Vulture (website)|Vulture]]|date=December 5, 2014|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-access=limited}}</ref> Lin confirmed that Fukunaga would begin [[principal photography]] in Summer 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/stephen-kings-it-remake-put-on-indefinite-hold-as-director-cary-fukunaga-walks-out-10275542.html|title=Stephen King's It remake put on indefinite hold as director Cary Fukunaga walks out|last=Shepherd|first=Jack|work=[[The Independent]]|date=May 26, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161007150949/http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/stephen-kings-it-remake-put-on-indefinite-hold-as-director-cary-fukunaga-walks-out-10275542.html|archive-date=October 7, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nOn February 3, 2015, Fukunaga was interviewed by ''[[Slate (magazine)|Slate]]'' wherein he spoke about ''It'', while mentioning he has someone in mind for the role of Pennywise.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.slate.com/blogs/browbeat/2015/02/03/cary_fukunaga_on_true_detective_season_2_his_adaption_of_stephen_king_s.html|title=Cary Fukunaga on Adapting It, His Musical With Owen Pallett, and #TrueDetectiveSeason2|last=Wickman|first=Forrest|work=[[Slate (magazine)|Slate]]|date=February 3, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160628135946/http://www.slate.com/blogs/browbeat/2015/02/03/cary_fukunaga_on_true_detective_season_2_his_adaption_of_stephen_king_s.html|archive-date=June 28, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On March 3, 2015, Fukunaga spoke of the film, particularly noting his goal to find the \"perfect guy to play Pennywise\". Fukunaga also revealed that he, Kajganich and Palmer had changed the names and dates in the script, adding, the spirit is similar to what he'd like to see in cinemas.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3334554/director-seeks-perfect-pennywise-clown/|title='It' Director Seeks \"Perfect Pennywise\" Clown|last=Disgusting|first=Mr|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=March 3, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160624183418/https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3334554/director-seeks-perfect-pennywise-clown/|archive-date=June 24, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On May 4, 2015, it was officially announced that [[Will Poulter]] had been cast to play Pennywise, after Fukunaga was \"blown away\" by his audition.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.ew.com/article/2015/05/04/will-poulter-it-pennywise|title=Will Poulter cast as Pennywise in Cary Fukunaga's It|last=P. Sullivan|first=Kevin|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=May 4, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160618220510/http://www.ew.com/article/2015/05/04/will-poulter-it-pennywise|archive-date=June 18, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref name=\"WillP\">{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2015/film/news/will-poutler-pennywise-the-clown-in-new-lines-it-remake-1201446495/|title=Will Poulter to Play the Evil Clown in 'It' Remake (EXCLUSIVE)|last=Kroll|first=Justin|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=May 4, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160629051959/https://variety.com/2015/film/news/will-poutler-pennywise-the-clown-in-new-lines-it-remake-1201446495/|archive-date=June 29, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> [[Ty Simpkins]] was considered to play one of The Losers' Club members.<ref name=\"Ty\">{{cite web|url=http://movieweb.com/jurassic-world-interview-ty-simpkins/|title=Jurassic World Interview with Ty Simpkins|last=Gallagher|first=Brian|work=[[MovieWeb]]|date=February 27, 2016|access-date=October 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161025114439/http://movieweb.com/jurassic-world-interview-ty-simpkins/|archive-date=October 25, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nOn May 25, 2015, it was reported that Fukunaga had dropped out as the director of ''It''.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2015/film/news/it-cary-fukunaga-director-exits-1201504672/|title='It' Loses Director Cary Fukunaga|last=Kroll|first=Justin|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=May 25, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160709011956/https://variety.com/2015/film/news/it-cary-fukunaga-director-exits-1201504672/|archive-date=July 9, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> According to [[TheWrap]], Fukunaga clashed with the studio and didn't want to compromise his artistic vision in the wake of budget cuts by New Line, which greenlit the first film at $30&nbsp;million.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://thewrap.com/cary-fukunaga-out-as-director-of-stephen-kings-it-at-new-line-exclusive/|title=Cary Fukunaga Out as Director of Stephen King's 'It' at New Line (Exclusive)|last=Geier|first=Thom|work=[[The Wrap]]|date=May 25, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160628034157/https://www.thewrap.com/cary-fukunaga-out-as-director-of-stephen-kings-it-at-new-line-exclusive/|archive-date=June 28, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> However, Fukunaga maintained that wasn't the case, with him stating he had bigger disagreements with New Line over the direction of the story: \"I was trying to make an unconventional horror film. It didn't fit into the algorithm of what they knew they could spend and make money back on based on not offending their standard genre audience.\"<ref name=Cary>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2015/film/news/cary-fukunaga-it-exit-1201584416/|title=Cary Fukunaga Offers New Details on Why 'It' Remake Fell Apart|last=Setoodeh|first=Ramin|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=September 2, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160704095044/https://variety.com/2015/film/news/cary-fukunaga-it-exit-1201584416/|archive-date=July 4, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> He made mention that the budget was perfectly fine, as well as his desire to make Pennywise more than just the clown.<ref name=Cary/> Fukunaga concluded by stating, \"We invested years and so much anecdotal storytelling in it. Chase and I both put our childhood in that story. So our biggest fear was they were going to take our script and bastardize it so I'm actually thankful that they are going to rewrite the script. I wouldn't want them to stealing our childhood memories and using that. I was honoring King's spirit of it, but I needed to update it. King saw an earlier draft and liked it.\"<ref name=Cary/><ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.ew.com/article/2015/08/17/cary-fukunaga-it-movie?hootPostID=b5145d9e2c7e687d8867d1c08604632f|title=Cary Fukunaga opens up about IT departure \u2013 Exclusive|last=P. Sullivan|first=Kevin|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=August 17, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161108110348/http://www.ew.com/article/2015/08/17/cary-fukunaga-it-movie?hootPostID=b5145d9e2c7e687d8867d1c08604632f|archive-date=November 8, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On Fukunaga's departure, King wrote, \"The remake of ''IT'' may be dead or undead but we'll always have [[Tim Curry]]. He's still floating down in the sewers of Derry.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/stephenking/status/602931191281496064|title=The remake of IT may be dead|last=King|first=Stephen|work=Twitter|date=May 25, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160322192030/https://twitter.com/StephenKing/status/602931191281496064|archive-date=March 22, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://news.sky.com/story/1490944/it-remake-dead-as-director-walks-away |title=It Remake 'Dead' As Director Walks Away |authors=Sky News Editors |work=[[Sky News]]|date=May 26, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150528215629/http://news.sky.com/story/1490944/it-remake-dead-as-director-walks-away |archive-date=May 28, 2015 |df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\n=== Andy Muschietti (2015\u20132017) ===\n{{quote box|align=right|width=35%|quote=\"...the way Cary intended to execute the script is something that only he can talk about. I can say my version of ''It'' highly emphasizes Pennywise's most terrifying virtue, which is it's ability to materialize into your worse fear; I want to take people in a journey into Pennywise's world through a disturbing, surrealistic and intoxicating experience that will leave nobody at ease.\"|source= \u2013 Andy Muschietti, on his version of ''It''.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.liljas-library.com/article.php?id=4659|title=IT Emphasizes Pennywise's Most Terrifying Virtue|last=Jorissen|first=Matt|work=Lilja's Library|date=November 6, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160808225514/http://www.liljas-library.com/article.php?id=4659|archive-date=August 8, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>}}\nOn July 16, 2015, it was announced that Andy Muschietti was in negotiations to direct ''It'', with New Line beginning a search for a new writer to tailor a script to Muschietti's vision,<ref name=\"Andr\u00e9s\">{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/stephen-kings-finds-new-director-809080|title=Stephen King's 'It' Finds New Director (Exclusive)|last=Kit|first=Borys|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=July 16, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160716124053/https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/stephen-kings-finds-new-director-809080|archive-date=July 16, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://empireonline.com/people/andres-muschietti/mama-andres-muschietti-negotiations-direct/|title=Mama's Andr\u00e9s Muschietti in Negotiations To Direct It|last=White|first=James|work=[[Empire (film magazine)|Empire]]|date=July 17, 2015|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161003180808/https://empireonline.com/people/andres-muschietti/mama-andres-muschietti-negotiations-direct/|archive-date=October 3, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> with the announcement also confirming the possible participation of Muschietti's sister, Barbara Muschietti, as a producer, and Richard Brener joining Hamada, Neustadter and Kuykendall to oversee the project.<ref name=\"Andr\u00e9s\"/> On April 22, 2016, it was indicated that Will Poulter, who was originally tapped to portray Pennywise in Fukunaga's version, had dropped out of the film due to a scheduling conflict and that executives were meeting with actors to portray the antagonist.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2016/film/news/warner-bros-announces-release-date-for-it-1201759274/|title=Warner Bros. Announces Release Date for 'It'|last=Kroll|first=Justin|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=April 22, 2016|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160625020838/https://variety.com/2016/film/news/warner-bros-announces-release-date-for-it-1201759274/|archive-date=June 25, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On April 22, 2016, New Line Cinema set the film for a release of September 8, 2017.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2016/04/chips-it-warner-bros-release-dates-2017-1201742518/|title=Warner Bros. Announces Release Date for 'It'|last=Kroll|first=Justin|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=April 22, 2016|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160625020838/https://variety.com/2016/film/news/warner-bros-announces-release-date-for-it-1201759274/|archive-date=June 25, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nOn October 30, 2015, Muschietti was interviewed by ''Variety'' wherein he spoke about his vision of ''It'', while mentioning Poulter was still in the mix for the role of Pennywise: \"Poulter would be a great option. For me he is at the top of my list.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2015/film/global/muschiettis-to-produce-supernatural-thriller-shadows-exclusive-1201630876/|title=Muschiettis to Produce Supernatural Thriller 'Shadows' (EXCLUSIVE)|last=Mayorga|first=Emilio|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=October 30, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160305002513/https://variety.com/2015/film/global/muschiettis-to-produce-supernatural-thriller-shadows-exclusive-1201630876/|archive-date=March 5, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> He confirmed that next summer is the time for them to start shooting. It was decided to shoot ''It'' during the summer months to give them the time to work with the children who have the main roles in the first part of the film.{{citation needed|date=April 2021}} Muschietti went on to say that \"King described 50s' terror iconography,\" adding that he feels there is a whole world now to \"rediscover, to update.\" He said there won't be any mummies or werewolves and that the \"terrors are going to be a lot more surprising.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3368274/stephen-kings-it-to-film-next-summer/|title=Stephen King's 'It' to Film Next Summer!|last=Disgusting|first=Mr|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=October 31, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160705165415/https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3368274/stephen-kings-it-to-film-next-summer/|archive-date=July 5, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On February 19, 2016, at the [[D.I.C.E. Summit|D.I.C.E. Summit 2016]] producer Roy Lee confirmed that Fukunaga and Chase Palmer's original script had been rewritten, with Lee remarking, \"It will hopefully be shooting later this year. We just got the California tax credit Dauberman wrote the most recent draft working with Muscetti, so it's being envisioned as two movies.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://screenrant.com/stephen-king-it-movies-filming-2016/|title=Stephen King's It May Start Filming in 2016; Two Movies Still Planned|last=Jones|first=Mike|work=Screen Rant|date=February 19, 2016|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160625070804/https://screenrant.com/stephen-king-it-movies-filming-2016/|archive-date=June 25, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nOn May 5, 2016, in an interview with ''[[Collider (website)|Collider]]'', David Kajganich expressed uncertainty as to whether drafts of his original screenplay would be used by Dauberman and Muschietti,<ref name=Kajganich/> with the writer stating, \"We know there's a new director, I don't know myself whether he's going back to any of the previous drafts or writing from scratch. I may not know until the film comes out. I don't know how it works! If you find out let me know.\"<ref name=Kajganich>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/david-kajganich-a-bigger-splash-it-movie-interview/|title='A Bigger Splash' Writer David Kajganich on His Unique Approach to the Remake and 'It'|last=Page|first=Aubrey|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=May 5, 2016|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160710194841/http://collider.com/david-kajganich-a-bigger-splash-it-movie-interview/|archive-date=July 10, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nOn June 2, 2016, [[Jaeden Lieberher]] was confirmed to be portraying lead protagonist, Bill Denbrough.<ref name=\"William\"/> On June 2, 2016, ''The Hollywood Reporter'' reported that [[Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd]] was in final negotiations to star as Pennywise, whose cast will also include [[Finn Wolfhard]], [[Jack Dylan Grazer]], [[Wyatt Oleff]], [[Chosen Jacobs]] and [[Jeremy Ray Taylor]].<ref name=Bill/> On June 2, 2016, there was a call for 100 background performers, with the background actor call going from 3 p.m. to 7 p.m. and by 4 p.m. more than 300 people had gone through; the casting call also asked for a marching band and period cars between 1970 and 1989.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.northumberlandnews.com/community-story/6704271-hundreds-turn-up-for-stephen-king-s-it-background-actor-cast-call-in-port-hope//|title=Hundreds turn up for Stephen King's 'It' background actor cast call in Port Hope |authors=Northumberland News Editor |work=Northumberland News|date=June 2, 2016|access-date=July 10, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160707232022/http://www.northumberlandnews.com/community-story/6704271-hundreds-turn-up-for-stephen-king-s-it-background-actor-cast-call-in-port-hope/|archive-date=July 7, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On February 18, 2016, ''The Hollywood Reporter'' reported that Owen Teague was set to portray Patrick Hocksetter.<ref name=Hockstetter/> On June 21, 2016, it was officially announced that [[Nicholas Hamilton]] had been cast to play Henry Bowers.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2016/06/nicholas-hamilton-joins-stephen-kings-it-the-last-film-festival-gets-theatrical-release-dennis-hopper-1201776453/|title=Nicholas Hamilton in Stephen King's 'It'; Monterey Media Acquires 'The Last Film Festival'|last=Busch|first=Anita|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=June 21, 2016|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160626085111/https://deadline.com/2016/06/nicholas-hamilton-joins-stephen-kings-it-the-last-film-festival-gets-theatrical-release-dennis-hopper-1201776453/|archive-date=June 26, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On June 21, 2016, [[Bloody Disgusting]] reported that [[Javier Botet]] was added to the cast shortly before filming commenced.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3395895/horror-wizard-javier-botet-to-haunt-mummy-stephen-kings/|title=Horror Wizard Javier Botet to Haunt 'The Mummy' and Stephen King's 'It'|last=Barkan|first=Jonathan|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=June 21, 2016|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160625030644/https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3395895/horror-wizard-javier-botet-to-haunt-mummy-stephen-kings/|archive-date=June 25, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://dreadcentral.com/news/172993/creature-performer-javier-botet-joins-mummy-stephen-kings/|title=Creature Performer Javier Botet Joins The Mummy and Stephen King's It|last=Squires|first=John|work=[[Dread Central]]|date=June 22, 2016|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160623161735/https://dreadcentral.com/news/172993/creature-performer-javier-botet-joins-mummy-stephen-kings/|archive-date=June 23, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On June 22, 2016, ''[[Deadline Hollywood]]'' reported that Muschietti had chosen actress [[Sophia Lillis]] to portray Beverly Marsh.<ref name=Beverly>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2016/06/it-new-line-sophia-lillis-stephen-king-aunjanue-ellis-pimp-1201777627/|title=Sophia Lillis Joins New Line's 'It' Remake;
