Lincoln|first=Ross|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=June 22, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160627162517/https://deadline.com/2016/06/it-new-line-sophia-lillis-stephen-king-aunjanue-ellis-pimp-1201777627/|archive-date=June 27, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On June 24, 2016, [[Moviepilot]] reported that Stephen Bogaert was added to the cast shortly before filming commenced, with Bogaert portraying Al Marsh, the abusive father of Beverly Marsh.<ref name=Bogaert>{{cite web|url=http://moviepilot.com/posts/3978236|title=Here's The Full Cast List for the New 'IT' Movie|last=Richardson|first=Jancy|work=[[Moviepilot]]|date=June 24, 2015|access-date=June 28, 2016|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160629070642/http://moviepilot.com/posts/3978236|archive-date=June 29, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nOn July 22, 2016, Barbara Muschietti was interviewed by ''Northumberland News''{{'}} Karen Longwell, wherein she spoke about the filming locations on ''It'', while mentioning the beauty of Port Hope being one of the reasons as to why it was chosen, while Muschietti added, \"We were looking for an idyllic town, one that would be a strong contrast to the story. Port Hope is the kind of place we all wish we had grown up in: long summers riding bicycles, walks by the lake, a lovely main street, charming homes with green lawns, warm people.\"<ref name=Criss/> Muschietti also mentioned that 360 extras from the area, from adults to tiny kids, had been involved.<ref name=Criss/>\n\nOn August 11, 2016, at [[The CW]] [[TCA Awards|TCA]] presentation for the upcoming series ''[[Frequency (TV series)|Frequency]]'', producer Dan Lin spoke of the piece's comparison to [[Netflix]]'s ''[[Stranger Things (TV series)|Stranger Things]]'', with Lee describing ''It'' being a \"homage to 80s movies\", while remarking: \"I think a great analogy is actually Stranger Things, and we're seeing it on Netflix right now. It's very much an homage to '80s movies, whether it's classic Stephen King or even [[Steven Spielberg|Spielberg]]. Think about ''[[Stand by Me (film)|Stand by Me]]'' (1986) as far as the bonding amongst the kids. But there is a really scary element in Pennywise.\"<ref name=Stranger>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-movie-stranger-things-dan-lin/|title='It' Producer Dan Lin Says the Remake Is Like 'Stranger Things'|last=Foutch|first=Haleigh|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=August 11, 2016|access-date=August 13, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160812183907/http://collider.com/it-movie-stranger-things-dan-lin/|archive-date=August 12, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Lin continued, speaking of how well the young cast has bonded in these first weeks of shooting. Lin stated, \"We clearly had a great dynamic amongst the kids. Really great chemistry is always a challenging thing with a movie like It because you're casting kids who don't have a ton of experience, but it ended up being really natural. Each kid, like a ''[[The Goonies]]'' (1985) or ''Stand by Me'' (1986), has a very specific personality and they're forming the loser's club obviously We've spent a few months getting the kids to bond and now they're going to fight this evil, scary clown.\"<ref name=Stranger/>\n\nOn February 9, 2017, at the press day for ''[[The Lego Batman Movie]]'' (2017), Lin confirmed that ''It'' is going to be rated R by the [[Motion Picture Association of America|MPAA]], to which  he stated to Collider.com{{'}}s Steve Weintraub, \"If you're going to make a \"Rated-R movie\", you have to fully embrace what it is, and you have to embrace the source material. It is a scary clown that's trying to kill kids. They do have a scary clown that's taken over the town of Derry, so it's going to be rated R.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-remake-rated-r-sequel-adults/#pennywise|title=Producer Dan Lin Confirms 'It' Rating and Sequel Plans|last=Goldberg|first=Matt|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=February 9, 2017|access-date=March 12, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170313125903/http://collider.com/it-remake-rated-r-sequel-adults/#pennywise|archive-date=March 13, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On March 11, 2017, Muschietti, at the [[SXSW]] festival, spoke of an element of the [[pre-production]] phase in his attempt to keep Skarsg\u00e5rd separated from the film's child actors, wherein the actor wasn't introduced to the young cast until Pennywise's first encounter with the children:<ref>{{cite web|url=https://dailydead.com/sxsw-2017-impressions-first-footage-new-footage-annabelle-2/|title=SXSW 2017: Impressions of First Footage from IT & New Footage from ANNABELLE 2|last=Wixson|first=Heather|work=Daily Dead|date=March 12, 2017|access-date=March 12, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170313131627/http://dailydead.com/sxsw-2017-impressions-first-footage-new-footage-annabelle-2/|archive-date=March 13, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> \"It was something that we agreed on, and that's how it happened. The day that he showed up on the stage, they fucking freaked out. Bill is like, seven-foot high, and I can't describe how scary he looks in person. He's a wiry man, crouching, making sounds, snotting, drooling, speaking in [[Swedish language|Swedish]] sometimes. Terrifying.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theverge.com/2017/3/12/14897214/it-reboot-pennywise-preview-sxsw-2017|title=The new Pennywise terrified the young cast of Stephen King's IT reboot|last=Farokhmanesh|first=Megan|work=[[The Verge]]|date=March 12, 2017|access-date=March 12, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170312200748/http://www.theverge.com/2017/3/12/14897214/it-reboot-pennywise-preview-sxsw-2017|archive-date=March 12, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Muschietti stated that the story had been moved forward, with the scenes with the young Losers Club shifting from the 1950s to the 1980s, while also describing their plot as \"getting much wider,\" with new material not in the novel or the [[It (miniseries)|1990 miniseries]].<ref name=\"SXSW\">{{cite web|url=http://www.austinchronicle.com/daily/sxsw/2017-03-12/sxsw-panel-face-your-fears/|title=SXSW Panel: Face Your Fears|last=Whittaker|first=Richard|work=[[The Austin Chronicle]]|date=March 12, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> However, Muschietti said he hoped it would still strike the same emotional resonance that the book did for him when he first read it: \"It's all about trying to hit the core and the heart.\"<ref name=SXSW/>\n\nOn July 12, 2017, Muschietti, in an interview with French magazine ''Mad Movies'', spoke of when developing the R rated film, in which allowed him to go into very adult themes, which was championed from the people at New Line Cinema.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.mad-movies.com/fr/module/99999735/4495/ca-d-andy-muschietti|title=\u00c7A BY ANDY MUSCHIETTI|authors=Mad Movies Editors|work=Mad Movies|date=July 12, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|archive-date=July 23, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180723003528/https://www.mad-movies.com/fr/module/99999735/4495/ca-d-andy-muschietti|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3444929/new-pennywise-image-found-french-magazine-cover/|title=New Pennywise Image Found On French Magazine Cover|last=Squires|first=John|work=[[Bloody 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> He also stated that, \"if you aimed for a PG-13 movie, you had nothing at the end. So we were very lucky that the producers didn't try to stop us. In fact it's more our own moral compass that sometimes showed us that some things lead us in places where we didn't want to go.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3446886/andy-muschietti-talks-holding-nothing-back-r-rated/|title=Andy Muschietti Talks Holding Nothing Back for \"R\"-rated 'IT'|last=Squires|first=John|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=July 14, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170716093735/https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3446886/andy-muschietti-talks-holding-nothing-back-r-rated/|archive-date=July 16, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.flickeringmyth.com/2017/07/it-director-andy-muschietti-on-the-films-r-rating/|title=It director Andy Muschietti on the film's R rating|last=Collinson|first=Gary|work=Flickering Myth|date=July 16, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> In the same interview, on July 12, 2017, producer Barbara Muschietti added that there was only one scene that was deemed to be too horrific to feature in the new adaptation, in which she stated,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.unilad.co.uk/film/new-it-film-will-contain-scenes-too-intense-for-the-original/|title=New IT Film Will Contain Scenes 'Too Intense' For The Original|last=Murray|first=Emily|work=[[UniLad]]|date=July 16, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|archive-date=August 8, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170808033117/https://www.unilad.co.uk/film/new-it-film-will-contain-scenes-too-intense-for-the-original/|url-status=dead}}</ref> \"you won't find the scene where a kid has his back broken and is thrown in the toilets. 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nOn July 19, 2017, in an interview with ''Variety''{{'}}s Brent Lang, director Muschietti commented of the monstrous forms that It shall be taking, as well as noting the fact that they'll be very different from the incarnations present in King's story, in which he stated,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3448025/various-monsters-will-different-book/|title=Various Monsters in 'IT' Will Be Very Different from the Book|last=Squires|first=John|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=July 19, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170720010749/https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3448025/various-monsters-will-different-book/|archive-date=July 20, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> \"The story is the same, but there are changes in the things the kids are scared of. In the book they're children in the 50s, so the incarnations of the monsters are mainly from movies, so it's [[Larry Talbot|Wolf Man]], [[Imhotep (The Mummy)|the Mummy]], [[Frankenstein's monster|Frankenstein]], and [[Count Dracula|Dracula]]. I had a different approach. I wanted to bring out deeper fears, based not only on movie monsters but on childhood traumas.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://joblo.com/horror-movies/news/director-says-stephen-king-s-it-will-not-feature-the-classic-movie-monsters-641|title=ANDY MUSCHIETTI TALKS IT PART 2 & CLASSIC MOVIE MONSTERS|last=Sprague|first=Mike|work=[[JoBlo.com]]|date=July 19, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.joe.co.uk/entertainment/theres-new-terrifying-details-about-the-it-film-134555|title=There's new terrifying details about the IT film|last=Moore|first=Paul|work=[[Joe (website)|Joe]]|date=July 20, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170720120650/https://www.joe.co.uk/entertainment/theres-new-terrifying-details-about-the-it-film-134555|archive-date=July 20, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> While on the topic of what being the key to a successful horror film, Muschietti concluded by remarking that \"Stay true to what scares you. If you don't respect that, you can't scare anyone.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/it-director-andres-muschietti-two-movies-bill-skarsgard-1202499038/amp/|title='It' Director on Tackling the Two R-Rated Movies and Why He Picked Bill Skarsgard for Pennywise|last=Lang|first=Brent|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=July 19, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170719214312/https://variety.com/2017/film/news/it-director-andres-muschietti-two-movies-bill-skarsgard-1202499038/amp/|archive-date=July 19, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Muschietti explained how Skarsg\u00e5rd caught his attention to embody Pennywise, while pointing out that he didn't want the young cast to spend too much time with the actor when not shooting, and encouraged the cast to \"maintain distance\" between them, wherein Muschietti detailed:<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.femalefirst.co.uk/movies/movie-news/andres-muschietti-confirms-prep-date-sequel-1075855.html|title=Andres Muschietti confirms prep date for IT sequel |authors=Female First Editors |work=Female First|date=July 20, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.msn.com/en-gb/entertainment/movies/andres-muschietti-confirms-prep-date-for-it-sequel/ar-AAoulDR|title=Andres Muschietti confirms prep date for IT sequel |authors=MSN Editors |work=[[MSN]]|date=July 20, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170808033345/http://www.msn.com/en-gb/entertainment/movies/andres-muschietti-confirms-prep-date-for-it-sequel/ar-AAoulDR|archive-date=August 8, 2017|url-status=dead}}</ref> We wanted to carry the impact of the encounters to when the cameras were rolling. The first scene where Bill interacted with the children, it was fun to see how the plan worked. The kids were really, really creeped out by Bill. He's pretty intimidating because he's six-four and has all this makeup.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://popculture.com/movies/2017/07/19/stephen-kings-it-remake-pennywise-bill-skarasgard/|title=Stephen King's 'It' Director Explains How Bill Skarsgard Won Coveted Pennywise Role|last=Cavanaugh|first=Patrick|work=Pop Culture|date=July 19, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017}}</ref>\n\n===Filming===\n[[File:Port Hope Town Hall.JPG|270x202px|left|thumbnail|[[Port Hope, Ontario|Port Hope]] had undergone a number of changes to transform it into the town of [[Derry (Stephen King)|Derry]].]]\n[[Production designer]] Mara LePere-Schloop went to [[Bangor, Maine]], to scope out locations including the [[Thomas Hill Standpipe]], the land running alongside the [[Kenduskeag Stream]] that in ''It'' is called The Barrens, it was confirmed on March 31, 2015, and the Waterworks on the [[Penobscot River]].<ref name=Bangor>{{cite Park]], US flags now hang in place of Canadian flags downtown, and [[Capitol Theatre (Port Hope)|Port Hope Capitol Theatre]] had appeared to be showing ''[[Batman (1989 film)|Batman]]'' (1989) and ''[[Lethal Weapon 2]]'' (1989), thus confirming the film's setting of 1989.<ref>{{cite 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> with an altered shooting schedule occurring from June 27 to September 21, 2016, and ultimately with [[post-production]] initially beginning on September 14, 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://addictedtohorrormovies.com/2016/09/23/filming-on-andy-muschiettis-remake-of-stephen-kings-it-has-wrapped/|title=Filming on Andy Muschietti's Remake of Stephen King's 'It' has Wrapped |authors=Addicted to Horror Movies Editors |work=Addicted to Horror Movies|date=September 23, 2016|access-date=September 28, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161002083417/https://addictedtohorrormovies.com/2016/09/23/filming-on-andy-muschiettis-remake-of-stephen-kings-it-has-wrapped/|archive-date=October 2, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\n===Cinematography===\n{{quote box|align=right|width=35%|quote=\"One of my main quests is highlighting the eyes of the actors, indeed. I believe that what is captured in the eye goes beyond what can be seen in facial expressions alone. So I always look for a specific way to highlight the eyes of each actor. We did several tests on Pennywise's eyes during camera tests and in the end, I used a flashlight. We tested a lot of different lamps and I chose a particularly powerful one, which gave a very hard light. When Pennywise looks at the kids, I wanted his eyes to look more than his desire to eat them. I liked the idea that, in his eyes, we can see that he knows the fear he inflicts. A bit like when a mother looks hard at her children to scold them. More than just scary eyes, I thought that was what the character needed. So something had to be done to emphasize his look.\"|source= \u2014 Chung Chung-hoon, on the visual power of lighting eyes in ''It''.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cinemateaser.com/2017/09/71671-interview-chung-chung-hoon-directeur-de-la-photographie-de-ca|title=Interview: Chung Chung-hoon, Director of Photography at \u00c7A|website=Cinemateaser|last=Allin|first=Aur\u00e9lien|date=September 27, 2017|access-date=November 5, 2017}}</ref>}} ''It'' was photographed with [[Arri Alexa#Alexa XT|Arri Alexa XT Plus]] and [[Arri Alexa#Alexa Mini|Alexa Mini]]<ref name=\"ascmag.com\"/> in a [[Aspect ratio (image)|distributed aspect ratio]] of [[2.39:1]] by [[Chung Chung-hoon]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.geekexchange.com/news/new-line-plans-to-release-it-in-imax/|title=New Line Plans to Release IT in IMAX|last=Rodriguez|first=Josef|work=[[Geek Monthly]]|date=August 20, 2017|access-date=September 18, 2017}}{{Dead link|date=October 2022 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref> For photographic lens, Chung used [[Panavision]] G Series Anamorphic Prime, Angenieux Optimo,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.panavision.com/youll-float-too-stephen-kings-it|title=YOU'LL FLOAT TOO IN STEPHEN KING'S IT|last=Panavision Staff|work=[[Panavision]]|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=September 18, 2017}}</ref> and Primo Prime in which Chung stated is used \"when Muschietti wants to use a wider lens or needs more frame space for visual effects. The look of the lenses is nearly the same. I mix them a lot and it works well.\"<ref name=\"ascmag.com\">{{cite web|url=https://ascmag.com/articles/it-fear-itself|title=It: Fear Itself|website=[[American Cinematographer]]|last=Dillon|first=Mark|date=October 19, 2017|access-date=November 5, 2017}}</ref> Cinematographer Chung and director Muschietti's discussions on the lighting of ''It'' were of temperature, with Muschietti wanting a hot summer with everyone sweating all the time, while admiring characters with shine on their faces.<ref name=\"October\">{{cite web|url=https://theasc.com/articles/october-issue-of-ac-issue-arriving-soon|title=October Issue of AC Arriving Soon|website=[[American Cinematographer]] |authors=American Cinematographer Editors |date=September 15, 2017|access-date=November 5, 2017}}</ref> Both also discussed the balance of making something realistic, but with an element of intrigue that something is not right.<ref name=October/> Chung mulled over the notion of a period look for ''It'', but ultimately felt the 1980s feel was conveyed through Claude Par\u00e9's sets and the work of Janie Bryant, in which Chung stated: \"Trying to make a movie set in the 1980s look like the 1980s can be dangerous.\"<ref name=October/> Initially he had thought of photographing with 1980s lighting rules and gear, though later feeling it to be superfluous as Muschietti and he were trying to capture a natural look.<ref name=October/>\n\nMuschietti himself found mainstream 1980s lighting too artificial thus preferred to through windows and bounce off the floor, allowing him to convey a feeling of intimacy with the characters, while admiring the approach of unsettling backlights and soft lights.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.koreanfilm.or.kr/jsp/news/interview.jsp?blbdComCd=601019&mode=INTERVIEW_VIEW&seq=282|title=CHUNG Chung-hoon, Cinematographer of It|website=KoBiz|last=Soon-jin|first=SONG|date=September 19, 2017|access-date=November 5, 2017}}</ref> Chung spoke of his experience on ''[[Stoker (film)|Stoker]]'' (2013), which taught him how to light quickly using one source: \"I feel lucky because some directors will always say, Can you make more light? But this movie is very naturalistic. My responsibility is to the audience and to tell the story, and if you want this movie to scare people, a natural look is best.\"<ref name=October/>\n\n===Editing===\n{{quote box\n| align = left\n| width = 35%\n| quote = \"The final is two hours and nine minutes from memory, the first editor\u2019s assembly was three hours and forty minutes and then after the director\u2019s cut, we were hovering just under the three-hour mark. Then we went through studio notes and audience screenings to further work the cut. Not only are there film rhythms, but there are also filmmaker rhythms. Cutting a film is a marathon, not a sprint. You have to emotionally and physically pace yourself.\"\n| source = \u2014 Jason Ballantine, on the final theatrical cut in ''It''.<ref name=\"Benach\">{{cite web|url=http://fashionista.com/2016/11/loving-movie-costumes|title=THE 'LOVING' COSTUMES ARE JUST AS POWERFUL AND UNDERSTATED AS THE FILM|website=Fashionista|last=Soo Hoo|first=Fawnia|date=November 7, 2016|access-date=December 9, 2016}}</ref>\n}}\n[[Film editor]] [[Jason Ballantine]] spoke of the difference in pacing and rhythm that comes with horror in ''It'', in which a story like this was broken up into individual encounters with Pennywise for each of the characters, thus requiring a particular approach.<ref name=\"ProVideo\">{{cite web|url=https://www.provideocoalition.com/AOTC-IT|title=ART OF THE CUT with \"IT\" editor, Jason Ballantine, ASE|last=Hullfish|first=Steve|work=ProVideo Coalition|date=September 16, 2017|access-date=April 5, 2019}}</ref> Each segment had to have the appropriate rhythm and setup for the inevitable jump scare, to which he explained: \"We were definitely conscious of trying to mix the rhythms up. Each encounter became somewhat more elaborate for the jump-scare in terms of what was shot. The first assembly was massively long So it did mean that screen time had to be dropped, either through the tightening of existing sequences or even scene deletions.\"<ref name=ProVideo/> Ballantine also spoke of the key factors when cutting ''It'', which included King's novel, and [[Tommy Lee Wallace]]'s [[It (miniseries)|1990 miniseries]].<ref name=ProVideo/>\n\nIn approaching a scene for ''It'', Ballantine mapped out his day-to-day workflow from getting his dailies to sitting down with Muschietti looking through what he's pieced together.<ref name=\"PremiumBeat\">{{cite web|url=https://www.premiumbeat.com/blog/post-production-process-behind-it/|title=A Look Inside the Post-Production Process Behind \"It\"|last=Baker|first=Logan|work=PremiumBeat|date=September 21, 2017|access-date=April 5, 2019}}</ref> Upon receiving the dailies, Ballantine looked through the footage to see if he needs any pickups or reshoots to report back to set, resulting in Pearce Roemer, Elliott Traeger, Ferran Banchs and Daniel Miller to ensure all the footage had been copied over before returning the footage for formatting.<ref name=PremiumBeat/> From there, Ballantine asks his assistants to arrange the selects in script-order so that he can have a better understanding of the structure, as well as work at a faster pace without worrying about getting lost in the footage.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.creativeplanetnetwork.com/news-features/it-editor-aims-provoke-visceral-reaction-619331|title='It' Editor Aims to Provoke 'Visceral Reaction' |authors=Creative Planet Network Editors |work=Creative Planet Network|date=September 17, 2017|access-date=April 5, 2019}}</ref><ref name=PremiumBeat/> Once Ballantine has a good chunk of the selects in the order he wants, the finished product from that batch will be about a third of the original length.<ref name=PremiumBeat/>\n\n===Design===\n====Costume design====\n[[File:Nicholas Hilliard 002.jpg|upright|right|thumbnail|[[It (character)|Pennywise]]'s gray costume was partly inspired by the clothing style of the [[Renaissance]].]]\nOn August 16, 2016, in an interview with ''[[Entertainment Weekly]]'', costume designer [[Katherine Jane Bryant|Janie Bryant]] spoke of crafting Pennywise's form-fitting suit and the inspirations to which it drew upon involving a number of bygone times among them the [[Medieval]], [[Renaissance]], [[Elizabethan era|Elizabethan]], and [[Victorian era|Victorian]] eras.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.yahoo.com/movies/it-first-look-a-new-close-up-of-pennywises-creepy-costume-154728395.html|title='It' First Look: A New Close-Up of Pennywise's Creepy Costume|last=Yahoo Movies Staff|work=[[Yahoo! Movies]]|date=August 16, 2016|access-date=August 20, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160824174714/https://www.yahoo.com/movies/it-first-look-a-new-close-up-of-pennywises-creepy-costume-154728395.html|archive-date=August 24, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Bryant explained that the costume incorporates all these otherworldly past lives, while highlighting the point that Pennywise is a clown from a different time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://uk.ign.com/articles/2016/08/16/it-movie-first-full-look-at-pennywise-the-clown|title=IT MOVIE: FIRST FULL LOOK AT PENNYWISE THE CLOWN|last=Osborn|first=Alex|work=[[IGN]]|date=August 16, 2016|access-date=August 20, 2016}}</ref> In designing Pennywise's costume, Bryant included a Fortuny [[pleating]], which gives the costume an almost a crepe-like effect,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.internationalpleating.com/what-is-the-difference-between-fortuny-pleating-and-mushroom-pleating/|title=What is the difference between Fortuny pleating and mushroom pleating?|last=K|first=George|work=Tom's Sons International Pleating|date=May 19, 2012|access-date=August 20, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160821054001/http://www.internationalpleating.com/what-is-the-difference-between-fortuny-pleating-and-mushroom-pleating/|archive-date=August 21, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> to which Bryant remarked, \"It's a different technique than what the Elizabethans would do. It's more organic, it's more sheer. It has a whimsical, floppy quality to it. It's not a direct translation of a ruff or a whisk, which were two of the collars popular during the Elizabethan period.\"<ref name=Costume>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.ew.com/article/2016/08/16/pennywise-costume-stephen-king-it-movie|title=Behold Pennywise the Clown's eerie costume from Stephen King's It|last=Breznican|first=Anthony|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=August 16, 2016|access-date=August 20, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160819040044/http://www.ew.com/article/2016/08/16/pennywise-costume-stephen-king-it-movie|archive-date=August 19, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nBryant played with multiple eras as a way of reflecting Pennywise's immortality and added a \"doll-like quality to the costume.\"<ref name=Costume/><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/pennywise-the-clown-it-new-film_us_57b3676be4b0b42c38aece0e|title=The First Look at Pennywise The Clown From The New 'It' Film Is Terrifying|last=Brucculieri|first=Julia|work=[[The Huffington Post]]|date=August 16, 2016|access-date=August 20, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160819234821/http://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/pennywise-the-clown-it-new-film_us_57b3676be4b0b42c38aece0e|archive-date=August 19, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> She furthered this by stating \"The pants being short, the high waistline of the jacket, and the fit of the costume is a very important element. It gives the character a child-like quality.\"<ref name=Costume/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/it-the-clown-pennywise-bill-skarsgard-stephen-king-stranger-things-andy-muschietti-a7194111.html|title=It: First full unsettling look at Pennywise the clown in Stephen King remake|last=Stolworthy|first=Jacob|work=[[The Independent]]|date=August 16, 2016|access-date=August 20, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160819185052/http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/it-the-clown-pennywise-bill-skarsgard-stephen-king-stranger-things-andy-muschietti-a7194111.html|archive-date=August 19, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Bryant spoke of the two puffs off the shoulder, sleeves and again on the [[Bloomers (clothing)|bloomers]], with her desire to create an \"organic, gourd or pumpkin kind of effect\", which includes the [[Overskirt|peplum]] at the waist, the flared, skirt-like fabric blossoming from below his doublet.<ref name=Costume/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.elizabethan-era.org.uk/elizabethan-doublets.htm|title=Elizabethan Doublets |authors=Elizabethan Doublets \u2013 Elizabethan Era Editors |work=Tom's Sons International Pleating|date=May 16, 2012|access-date=August 20, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160820192200/http://www.elizabethan-era.org.uk/elizabethan-doublets.htm|archive-date=August 20, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> She explains, \"It helps exaggerate certain parts of the body. The costume is very nipped in the waist and with the peplum and bloomers it has an expansive silhouette.\"<ref name=Costume/> The main color of his costume is a dusky gray, but with a few splashes of color.<ref name=Costume/> She concludes the interview by stating, \"The [[Pom-pom|pompoms]] are orange, and then with the trim around the cuffs and the ankles, it's basically a ball fringe that's a combination of orange, red, and cinnamon. It's almost like Pennywise fades into his environment. But there are accents to pull out the definition of the gray silk.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3403108/heres-pennywise-full-clown-costume-hes-definitely-freaky/|title='It': Here's \"Pennywise\" in Full Clown Costume and He's Definitely Freaky!|last=Barkan|first=Jonathan|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=August 16, 2016|access-date=August 20, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160819183605/https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3403108/heres-pennywise-full-clown-costume-hes-definitely-freaky|archive-date=August 19, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nBryant explained that she wished for Pennywise to have an organic element about himself, with herself paying attention to King's description of Pennywise as being in a silvery gray.<ref name=\"Collaborative\">{{cite web|url=https://window.brenau.edu/articles/fashion-film-and-a-flair-for-the-dramatics/|title=FASHION, FILM AND A FLAIR FOR THE DRAMATICS|last=Bowman|first=Kristen|work=The Brenau Collaborative|date=June 6, 2018|access-date=July 2, 2018}}</ref> For Pennywise, Bryant's manufacturer built 17 different clown costumes to accommodate the action in the film.<ref name=Collaborative/> Muschietti spoke of the fact that the entity of Pennywise has been around for thousands of years, thus from an esthetic standpoint wished to depart from the 20th century clown framework, in which he stated<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.flickeringmyth.com/2017/08/new-poster-for-stephen-kings-it-director-discusses-pennywise-design/|title=New poster for Stephen King's It, director discusses Pennywise design|last=Cranswick|first=Amie|work=Flickering Myth|date=August 25, 2017|access-date=August 30, 2017}}</ref> \"I think it looks cheap, and it's too related to social events and stuff and circus and stuff. Circus is fine, but I'm more aesthetically attracted to the old time, like the 19th century clown. And given that this guy has been around for centuries, I wondered myself why, why not, having an upgrade that was 1800s?\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://movieweb.com/it-movie-2017-why-stephen-king-wasnt-involved/|title=Why Stephen King Had Nothing to Do with the IT Movie|last=Scott|first=Ryan|work=[[MovieWeb]]|date=August 22, 2016|access-date=August 30, 2017}}</ref>\n\n====Production design====\n{{quote box\n| quote = \"One of the main sets that we worked on one of them was an evil house. The evil house had three specific moments there's the exterior, there's the interior, and then the basement, where the well is where Pennywise accesses the sewers and the cisterns where his lair is I also wanted to have this spooky tree looming at the house so we decided to build it until a crew member found this tree, driving to the office here one morning. So we bought the tree from the owner after negotiating.\"\n| source = \u2014 Claude Par\u00e9, on the construction of [[Derry (Stephen King)|29 Neibolt Street]] on ''It''.<ref name=\"Par\u00e9\">{{cite web|url=https://www.dreadcentral.com/news/243647/exclusive-visited-set-heres-saw/|title=Exclusive: We Visited the Set of IT and Here's What We Saw!|last=Buckley|first=Heather|work=[[Dread Central]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=August 13, 2017}}</ref>\n| width = 35%\n| align = right\n}}\n[[Production designer]] Claude Par\u00e9 commented that apart from [[Derry (Stephen King)#29 Neibolt Street|29 Neibolt Street]], that the other main component of Muschietti's ''It'' were both the sewers and the cistern, to which Muschietti and himself worked every morning for roughly three months observing,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://artdepartmental.com/2017/05/16/design-talks-an-evening-with-production-designer-claude-pare/|title=DESIGN TALKS: 5 Things I Learned from 'It' Production Designer Claude Par\u00e9|last=Lagac\u00e9|first=Rose|work=Art Departmental|date=May 16, 2017|access-date=August 13, 2017}}</ref> looking at the plans and attempting to figure out what was the best pattern for themselves on stages<ref>{{cite web|url=https://vimeo.com/224236557|title=Featuring Claude Par\u00e9, in conversation with DGC Designer John Blackie |authors=Directors Guild of Canada Editors |work=[[Directors Guild of Canada]]|date=April 1, 2017|access-date=August 13, 2017}}</ref> they had access to a rather precise stage, though having to make profit as much as they could, of what they had.<ref name=Par\u00e9/> Par\u00e9 discussed about knowing that Muschietti and himself had to have a culvert entrance in The Barrens, somewhere in or around [[Toronto]].<ref name=Par\u00e9/>\n\nThe construction of 29 Neibolt Street was one of the great challenges of the production, with Par\u00e9 later explaining he wanted the haunted house of the film to be visually strong and in line with the decor of the great films of the horror genre such as the Bates house from ''[[Psycho (1960 film)|Psycho]]'' (1960), or the Overlook Hotel of ''[[The Shining (film)|The Shining]]'' (1980).<ref name=\"Neibolt\">{{cite web|url=http://www.journaldemontreal.com/2017/08/30/un-quebecois-dans-le-generique-de-ica-i|title=A Qu\u00e9b\u00e9cois in the credits of \u00c7a|last=Demers|first=Maxime|work=Le Journal de Montr\u00e9al|date=August 30, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> Par\u00e9 worked extensively with Muschietti to imagine a haunted house that unleashes a presence that is discovered to be a character in its own right.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://quebec.huffingtonpost.ca/2017/09/06/claude-parre-decors-film-ca_a_23198720/|title=Quebecer Claude Par\u00e9 behind the scenery of the film \"\u00c7a\"|last=Houdassine|first=Isma\u00ebl|work=[[HuffPost]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> The exterior of 29 Neibolt Street was built in [[Oshawa|Oshawa, Ontario]], with the interior scenes being filmed in a former hospice.<ref name=Neibolt/>\n\nSix months after principal photography, Par\u00e9 built the clown room on a sound-stage at [[Pinewood Toronto Studios]] as Muschietti felt the Neibolt Street sequence required more scares to which Par\u00e9 stated Muschietti had the concept of wanting to have clowns from different eras, in which Par\u00e9 said:<ref name=\"House\">{{cite web|url=https://syfy.com/syfywire/the-it-house-was-actually-a-creepy-haunted-house-irl-too|title=THE IT HOUSE WAS ACTUALLY A CREEPY HAUNTED HOUSE IRL, TOO|last=Zakarin|first=Jordan|work=[[Syfy]]|date=September 15, 2017|access-date=September 21, 2017}}</ref> \"There were real clowns and fake clowns. There was lots of work put into dressing mannequins and putting some heads on them with masks and wigs and so on. Some of them were real people, so they start moving as you see in the movie.\"<ref name=House/> Conceptually, Muschietti himself spoke of how he wished to keep the [[cistern]] more grounded and real, instead of going into a world of fantasy: \"I decided to do a compelling and surrealistic but still grounded physical place.\"<ref name=House/> Par\u00e9 originally had wished that the sewers were composed of bricks, due to it being of more period-accuracy, however, the cost was deemed too great thus his team and himself decided to go with formed concrete which was constructed with a mixture of planks and plywood sheets.<ref name=Par\u00e9/> Par\u00e9 spoke of the special attention paid to the water drainage for the sewer, as well as the water marks that he said echoed those of [[New Orleans]] after [[Hurricane Katrina]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://editorial.rottentomatoes.com/article/clown-choreography-and-a-terrifying-gerber-baby-visiting-the-set-of-stephen-kings-it/|title=CLOWN CHOREOGRAPHY AND A TERRIFYING GERBER BABY: VISITING THE SET OF STEPHEN KING'S IT|last=Drake|first=Grae|work=[[Rotten Tomatoes]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=August 13, 2017}}</ref>\n\nPar\u00e9 later explained that his team looked at the location, with them later having kids climb up and down to which later resulted in the construction of the well on the stage, which connects Pennywise's tunnel, giving access to the tunnels, which in turn gives access to the cistern:<ref name=Par\u00e9/> \"which is the giant set that we're shooting now, and in which Pennywise has his wagon and on top of which there's a pile of all the clothes and toys of the dead kids over the many centuries.\"<ref name=Par\u00e9/> The vortex of dead children was also a creation of Muschietti and Par\u00e9, with floating being a \"metaphor for dying,\" according to Muschietti.<ref name=House/> Par\u00e9 had to get down to logistics with conversations taking place about how many bodies would be floating, as well as the speed at which the children were spinning around, with Par\u00e9 remarking:<ref name=House/> \"We didn't want to go over a year worth of kids, because all the kids that would have been dead would have been eaten in the 27 years that Pennywise was away So the kids of that era are basically a reserve for the next 27 years.\"<ref name=House/>\n\n====Sound design====\n[[Chris Jenkins (sound engineer)|Chris Jenkins]] and Michael Keller were [[sound engineer]]s for the film, tasked with [[sound mixing]], while sound editor [[Victor Ray Ennis]] supervised the process.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.wbsound.com/it-opens-with-a-13-5m-thursday-box-office/|title=\"IT\", opens with a $13.5M Thursday box office! |authors=Warner Bros. Sound Editors |work=[[Warner Bros.|Warner Bros. Sound]]|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> Director Muschietti was clear unto the sound engineers about every aspect of the soundscape, especially when it came to dynamics.<ref name=\"Sound\">{{cite web|url=https://www.izotope.com/en/blog/artist-stories/how-the-sound-designers-of-it-created-fear-with-sound.html|title=How the Sound Designers of 'It' Created Fear with Sound|last=Godowsky|first=Dave|work=[[iZotope]]|date=October 31, 2017|access-date=April 13, 2018}}</ref> During the final mix there were moments when Muschietti conducted the peaks and valleys of the sound design and score, to which [[sound designer]] Paul Hackner stated, \"It was in these moments when perceived silence, created by small transients such as water drips, foot creaks, or actual silence, were revealed, resulting in a dynamic mix.\"<ref name=Sound/>\n\n===Visual effects===\n{{quote box|align=left|width=35%|quote=\"Basically what they did was bring in all the stunt performers into a gym, and they learned the choreography and they motion-captured this. We built really quick CG assets for all the characters, including Pennywise, and we planned out all his transformations and the action. In the end, you could have the shape of both characters, but both of them could have the textures of one or the other. With some simulated effects we'd be able to balance all of that out and really time it to what [Muschietti] was looking for.|source= \u2014 Arnaud Brisebois, on the showdown with Pennywise in ''It''.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://syfy.com/syfywire/how-its-special-effects-team-made-pennywises-kill-mouth-and-invented-a-new-character|title=HOW IT'S SPECIAL EFFECTS TEAM MADE PENNYWISE'S KILL MOUTH AND INVENTED A NEW CHARACTER|website=[[Syfy]]|last=Failes|first=Ian|date=October 13, 2017|access-date=January 5, 2018|archive-date=January 29, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180129223215/http://www.syfy.com/syfywire/how-its-special-effects-team-made-pennywises-kill-mouth-and-invented-a-new-character|url-status=dead}}</ref>}}\n[[Nicholas Brooks (special effects artist)|Nicholas Brooks]] was the overall [[visual effects supervisor]] and the visual effects company [[Rodeo FX]] worked on most of the visual effects on ''It'',<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cinefex.com/upcomingfilms/upcoming.php?id=670|title=It |authors=Cinefex Editors |work=[[Cinefex]]|date=July 15, 2016|access-date=April 5, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170329045930/http://www.cinefex.com/upcomingfilms/upcoming.php?id=670|archive-date=March 29, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rodeofx.com/en/projects/it|title=IT - In Production |authors=Rodeo FX Editors |work=[[Rodeo FX]]|date=March 29, 2017|access-date=April 5, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170405170059/https://www.rodeofx.com/en/projects/it|archive-date=April 5, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rodeofx.com/en/filmography|title=FILMOGRAPHY |authors=Rodeo FX Editors |work=[[Rodeo FX]]|date=March 29, 2017|access-date=April 5, 2017|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170405170726/https://www.rodeofx.com/en/filmography|archive-date=April 5, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> completing 95 shots for the film.<ref name=\"Rodeo\">{{cite web|url=https://www.rodeofx.com/en/news/Rodeo-FX-brings-IT-to-life|title=Rodeo FX brings IT to life|last=Brisebois|first=Arnaud|work=[[Rodeo FX]]|date=September 12, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> ''Rodeo FX'' was tasked with creating a number of CG assets to either enhance or even completely replace Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd's Pennywise, amongst others being the giant abandoned cistern within the heart of Pennywise's lair.<ref name=Rodeo/> Both from a technical and creative standpoint, the various shapes created for Pennywise presented a large challenge for ''Rodeo FX''{{'}}s modeling, rigging and creature FX teams.<ref name=Rodeo/> The visual effects company Atomic Arts were initially brought in to create the paper boat sequence for ''It'', which covers much of the first trailers, to which all of the shots were used in the final film and the company were awarded many more shots in Muschietti's piece.<ref name=\"Atomic\">{{cite web|url=http://www.atomicarts.net/portfolio/recent-work/it/|title=Stephen Kings It|authors=Atomic Arts Editors|work=Atomic Arts|date=July 27, 2016|access-date=August 11, 2017|archive-date=January 15, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180115211023/http://www.atomicarts.net/portfolio/recent-work/it|url-status=dead}}</ref>  Atomic Arts highlighted the challenges in creating the paper boat sequence, as Muschietti and Chung shot in it bright sunshine.<ref name=Atomic/> [[Amalgamated Dynamics]] worked on the special makeup effects on ''It''.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.studioadi.com/filmography.php|title=Amalgamated Dynamics - Filmography |authors=Amalgamated Dynamics Editors |work=[[Amalgamated Dynamics]]|date=July 15, 2016|access-date=March 28, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170112121616/http://www.studioadi.com/filmography.php|archive-date=January 12, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\nProducer Barbara Muschietti stated that ''It'' would use [[computer-generated imagery]] as a support tool in every circumstance; never as an element standing on its own in regard to its relationship with [[practical effects]], to which she stated, \"In every film, in this day and age, there is some CG, but we will use it as little as possible.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.torontosun.com/2017/08/04/stephen-kings-pennywise-is-back-secrets-from-the-set-of-it|title=Stephen King's Pennywise is back: Secrets from the set of 'It'|last=Daniell|first=Mark|work=[[The Toronto Sun]]|date=July 15, 2016|access-date=March 28, 2017}}</ref> Andy Muschietti spoke of ''It'' containing a small amount of CGI, with much of Pennywise being Skarsg\u00e5rd and his face:<ref name=\"GQ\">{{cite web|url=https://www.gq.com/story/it-movie-andy-muschietti|title=How the Director of It Filmed Its Most Nightmare-Inducing Scene|last=Meslow|first=Scott|work=[[GQ]]|date=September 12, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> \"The rest it's a shape-shifting monster, and I wanted to bring that to the screen, when he's basically trying to throw everything he has at them.\", while signifying the importance of design and execution in the eternal discussion of practical versus CG.<ref name=GQ/>\n\n[[Company 3]]{{'}}s Stephen Nakamura collaborated with Muschietti to color grade ''It'', completing the film's digital intermediate in [[Blackmagic Design#Editing Software|Blackmagic DaVinci Resolve]] at [[EFILM]],<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.creativeplanetnetwork.com/news/post/it-hdr-darkness-scariest-all/619289|title=In 'It,' HDR Darkness is the Scariest of All|last=Altman|first=Randi|work=Creative Planet Network|date=September 22, 2017|access-date=September 26, 2017}}</ref> spoke of the concepts about the look of Muschietti's film that evolved during production, and while continuing it in the [[Digital intermediate|DI]], the idea that a lot of the film takes place in fairly high-key situations, not the kind of dark, shadowy world some horror films exist in.<ref name=\"Nakamura\">{{cite web|url=http://postperspective.com/colorist-stephen-nakamura-grading-stephen-kings/|title=Colorist Stephen Nakamura on grading Stephen King's It|last=Altman|first=Randi|work=postPerspective|date=September 11, 2017|access-date=September 18, 2017}}</ref> Nakamura said, \"It's a period piece. It's set in a small town that sort of looks like this pleasant place to be, but all this wild stuff is happening!\"<ref name=Nakamura/> On the work connected on Pennywise during the digital intermediate, Nakamura spoke of having alpha channel mattes cut around Pennywise's eyes for every shot he's in, while using the color corrector to make changes to his eyes:\"<ref name=Nakamura/> Other moments Nakamura mentioned was the battle between the kids and Pennywise underground, wherein the setting shifts the story into darkness, with such an effect working powerfully in the 14-footlambert standard digital cinema version and even more so in the 31-footlambert [[High-dynamic-range imaging|HDR]] pass which was completed for the film's [[Dolby Cinema]] version, in contrast to Nakamura's work on ''[[Tomorrowland (film)|Tomorrowland]]'' (2015), with him explaining:<ref name=Nakamura/> \"In the Dolby Cinema version, the scene can feel significantly darker but also contain more detail. You're pushing more light through the images overall and the contrast ratio is massive so dark scenes can be even darker but we can hold onto every scary detail. It's a very effective tool to have for this kind of movie.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://efilm.com/spotlights/09-08-2017/into-the-shadows-color-on-it-|title=INTO THE SHADOWS: COLOR ON \"IT\" |authors=EFILM Editors |work=[[EFILM]]|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=September 18, 2017}}</ref>\n\n==Themes==\n{{See also|It (novel)#Themes|It (miniseries)#It's content in relation to television restrictions}}\n''It'' is a [[Coming-of-age story|loss of innocence]] story with fear, mortality and survivalist themes.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://empireonline.com/people/stephen-king/new-images-pennywise-kids/|title=New Images Of Pennywise And The Kids From It|last=White|first=James|work=[[Empire (film magazine)|Empire]]|date=March 28, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170328191010/https://empireonline.com/people/stephen-king/new-images-pennywise-kids/|archive-date=March 28, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> Muschietti remarked of the film's elements of coming of age and issues of mortality, wherein he states such themes are prevalent in King's book, though that in reality these occur in a more progressive way,<ref name=Theme>{{cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/movies/2017/03/27/see-a-creepy-cool-pennywise-photo-from-stephen-king-it-movie-adaptation/99590666/|title=See a creepy/cool photo of the new Pennywise in Stephen King's 'It' remake|last=Truitt|first=Brian|work=[[USA Today]]|date=March 27, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170330224039/http://www.usatoday.com/story/life/movies/2017/03/27/see-a-creepy-cool-pennywise-photo-from-stephen-king-it-movie-adaptation/99590666/|archive-date=March 30, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> \"There's a passage in ''It'' that reads, 'Being a kid is learning how to live and being an adult is learning how to die.' There's a bit of a metaphor of that and it just happens in a very brutal way, of course.\"<ref name=Theme/>\n\nHe also mentioned the characterization of Pennywise's survivalist attitude, and a passage in the novel which inspired Muschietti, was when Bill wonders if Pennywise is eating children simply because that's what we're told monsters do, in stating,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://joblo.com/movie-news/andres-muschietti-spills-new-details-about-it-and-reveals-new-images-288|title=ANDR\u00c9S MUSCHIETTI SPILLS NEW DETAILS ABOUT IT AND REVEALS NEW IMAGES|last=Fraser|first=Kevin|work=[[JoBlo.com]]|date=March 27, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170401060237/https://joblo.com/movie-news/andres-muschietti-spills-new-details-about-it-and-reveals-new-images-288|archive-date=April 1, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> \"It's a tiny bit of information, but that sticks with you so much. Maybe it is real as long as children believe in it. And in a way, Pennywise's character is motivated by survival. In order to be alive in the imagination of children, he has to keep killing.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3429824/pennywise-losers-club-highlighted-new-images/|title=Pennywise and the Losers' Club Highlighted in New 'IT' Images|last=Squires|first=John|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=March 27, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170401143755/https://bloody-disgusting.com/news/3429824/pennywise-losers-club-highlighted-new-images/|archive-date=April 1, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://screencrush.com/new-it-images-pennywise/|title=New 'It' Images Feature a Red Balloon and a Bunch of Terrified|last=Stefansky|first=Emma|work=ScreenCrush|date=March 27, 2017|access-date=March 31, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170401060013/http://screencrush.com/new-it-images-pennywise/|archive-date=April 1, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> While Muschietti acknowledges it to be a horror film, he, too, felt that it's not simply just that: \"It's a story of love and friendship and a lot of other beautiful emotions.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://ew.com/movies/2017/07/20/pennywise-dis-arms-in-secret-comic-con-footage-from-stephen-kings-it/|title=Pennywise disarms in secret Comic-Con footage from Stephen King's It|last=Breznican|first=Anthony|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=July 20, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170721032217/http://ew.com/movies/2017/07/20/pennywise-dis-arms-in-secret-comic-con-footage-from-stephen-kings-it/|archive-date=July 21, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\n==Influences==\n{{quote box\n| align = right\n| width = 35%\n| quote = \"We were fans of horror at very early age; we were exposed to horror movies very early in life so there was this addiction we carried very early, and then came Stephen King. We're very big fans of his. He's my literary hero. It all started with ''[[Pet Sematary]]'' but then ''It'' came along and for me, it was a mind-blowing experience. My first reaction, when offered the opportunity to direct this movie, was basically to go back to my emotional experience reading the book when I was a child, and translating that into a movie that would blow my mind as an adult. Those were the big ideas when approaching the making of this movie.\"\n| source = \u2014 Andy Muschietti on King's influence in his approach to ''It''.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/it-movie-andy-muschietti-barbara-muschietti-stephen-king-remake-interview-1202159135/|title=Encore: How The Muschietti Siblings Turned Stephen King's Killer Clown Into The 'It' Movie Of Fall \u2013 Q&A|last=Fleming|first=Mike Jr.|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 9, 2017|access-date=October 6, 2017}}</ref>\n}} Director Andy Muschietti said influences on ''It'' included the \"visceral\" authority of horror cinema: ''[[The Howling (film)|The Howling]]'' (1981), ''[[The Thing (1982 film)|The Thing]]'' (1982), and ''[[Near Dark]]'' (1987).<ref name=\"Influences\">{{cite web|url=http://moviehole.net/2017122255interview-andres-and-barbara-muschietti-it|title=Interview : Andr\u00e9s and Barbara Muschietti \u2013 IT|last=Turney|first=Drew|work=Moviehole|date=August 28, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> He also spoke of the influential contributions of [[Clive Barker]] and [[John Carpenter]].<ref name=Influences/> He cited the influence of [[Steven Spielberg]] in \"the way of understanding story and filmmaking, because he has such a strong emotional element to all his stories.\", while crediting [[Stephen King]], alongside directors such as [Carpenter] and [[Joe Dante]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/features/it-interview-director-andy-muschietti-pennywise-stephen-king-adaptation-bill-skarsgard-chapter-ii-a7937366.html|title=It interview: Director Andy Muschietti on staying true to the spirit of Stephen King|last=Loughrey|first=Clarisse|work=[[The Independent]]|date=August 28, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> He also sought to emulate the whimsical and nostalgic perspective on childhood, while providing a balance with a much harsher viewpoint.<ref name=\"Childhood\">{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/andy-muschietti-it-movie-interview/|title=Andy Muschietti on 'IT' and Why Stephen King Wasn't Involved in the Film|last=Foutch|first=Haleigh|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=August 21, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> He stated: \"The movie, the tone of the movie regarding what childhood is and experiences of childhood is pretty wide. There's the Spielberg moments and there's the [[Larry Clark]] moments.\"<ref name=Childhood/>\n\nMuschietti spoke of bringing certain cultural experience within the genre to ''It'', in which he highlights his devotion to horror coming from international horror films and literature, to which he stated,<ref name=\"Storytelling\">{{cite web|url=https://www.vulture.com/2017/09/muschietti-siblings-talk-it-and-expressionist-bullies.html|title=It's Andy and Barbara Muschietti on Changing Cary Fukunaga's Script and Scaring Kids|last=Crucchiola|first=Jordan|work=[[Vulture (website)|Vulture]]|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017|url-access=limited}}</ref> \"there's other sides to my storytelling influences that comes from of course [[Jorge Luis Borges]] and [[Adolfo Bioy Casares]] and writers like [[Horacio Quiroga]] But you know, my love for horror comes from movies that were mainly English language.\"<ref name=Storytelling/> Muschietti based his portrayal of bullying in ''It'' as an homage to personal experience in the '80s with bullies, through the pure cruelty of Henry Bowers, where he speaks of them being very mean and very expressionist in their art of bullying, which is an aspect he wanted to explore.<ref name=Storytelling/> The sequence with Judith, the woman in the portrait whose form It assumes to terrify Stan, was based on Muschietti's experience with the paintings of [[Amedeo Modigliani]], one of which hung in Muschietti's childhood home, and which he found frightening, interpreting Modigliani's stylisation as monstrous.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://bloody-disgusting.com/movie/3458110/muschietti-talks-paintings-inspired-nightmarish-new-creature/|title=Muschietti Talks Paintings that Inspired Nightmarish New 'IT' Creature|last=Squires|first=John|work=[[Bloody Disgusting]]|date=September 10, 2017|access-date=September 18, 2017}}</ref>\n\nSkarsg\u00e5rd spoke of [[Heath Ledger]] as being an inspiration, while contrasting between Ledger's [[The Joker (The Dark Knight)|Joker]] and his Pennywise, in which he stated: \"I think the biggest difference between Pennywise and the Joker character or at least Heath Ledger's interpretation is that he's far more based in reality.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://ew.com/movies/2017/09/09/pennywise-joker-it-skarsgard-ledger/|title=It star Bill Skarsgard compares his Pennywise performance to Heath Ledger's Joker|last=Miller|first=Mike|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=September 9, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> He also sought to not attempt to emulate the performance in ''[[The Dark Knight (film)|The Dark Knight]]'' (2008), he remarked: \"I deliberately tried to make mine different because it's such a clear, iconic performance so I wanted to stray away from it as far as possible.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.heraldsun.com.au/entertainment/movies/bill-skarsgard-reveals-how-he-became-pennywise-the-clown-for-steven-kings-it-movie/news-story/b73f68c4ce512a448b8fed3ce3938554|title=Bill Skarsgard reveals how he became Pennywise the clown for Steven King's It movie|last=Wigney|first=James|work=[[The Herald Sun]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> Skarsg\u00e5rd studied animal programs to assist him in developing Pennywise's physical behavior, in which he zeroed in on the energy of hyenas and the lower-lip scowl of bears as touchstones.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/playback-podcast-bill-skarsgard-it-stephen-king-1202558033/|title=Playback: Bill Skarsgard on 'It' and Belching His Way Into Pennywise|last=Tapley|first=Kristopher|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=September 14, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> While speaking of the inexplicable nature of Pennywise, Skarsg\u00e5rd stated: \"Ledger's Joker is rooted in the real; you can break down the psychology. But Pennywise is not a real person.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.latimes.com/entertainment/movies/la-ca-mn-sneaks-it-pennywise-20170901-story.html|title='It's' new Pennywise actor Bill Skarsgard breaks down what makes the clown so scary|last=Zeitchik|first=Steven|work=[[The Los Angeles Times]]|date=September 1, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017|url-access=limited}}</ref> Skarsg\u00e5rd explained that Pennywise's succinct shuffles, whilst attacking and lunging toward his targets, were inspired by his little brother, Ossian, to which he stated: \"I don't know if you've seen kids run like this, but they move their arms way too fast, and it looks really, really funny. And I just loved the way my brother ran as a kid. It was just out of sync. So I incorporated that into the character, and you get this really explosive effect. It's really unsettling when it happens.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.rollingstone.com/movies/features/it-meet-the-man-behind-killer-clown-pennywise-w501071|title='It': Meet the Man Behind Killer Clown Pennywise|last=Suskind|first=Alex|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=September 11, 2017|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref>\n\nIn approaching the story, Barbara Muschietti referred to Stephen King's ''It'' (1986) as \"our bible\", while thinking it to be interesting to respect the proper chronology, with the Muschietti siblings going into the casting process with the book in mind.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-movie-barbara-muschietti-interview/|title='IT' Producer Barbara Muschietti Answers Burning Questions: Going Hard-R, Fukunaga's Script, 'Part 2' & More|last=Foutch|first=Haleigh|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=July 31, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> Muschietti spoke of using Fukunaga and Palmer's original screenplay as a basis, however, \"skewed it in a different direction\",<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-movie-cary-fukunaga-script-changes/|title='IT' Director Andy Muschietti Discusses the Changes from Cary Fukunaga's Draft|last=Foutch|first=Haleigh|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> to which her brother stated: \"It was a good script, in terms of characters and the depth of characters and such, but it didn't really tap into one of the most attractive traits of the character, which was the shape-shifting qualities.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://moviepilot.com/p/cary-fukunaga-script-stephen-king-it-movie-controversial/4362649|title=Why Did Director Cary Fukunaga Leave Stephen King's 'IT' Movie And What Was So Controversial About His Script?|last=Opie|first=David|work=[[Moviepilot]]|date=August 31, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> Screenwriter [[Gary Dauberman]] said influences on ''It'' included ''[[Stand by Me (film)|Stand by Me]]'' (1986),<ref name=\"Dauberman\">{{cite web|url=https://www.slashfilm.com/it-screenwriter-interview-gary-dauberman-on-adapting-stephen-kings-epic/|title='It' Screenwriter Gary Dauberman on Transforming a 1,000 Page Book Into a Movie [Interview]|last=Topel|first=Fred|work=[[/Film]]|date=August 31, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> while stating: \"that's one of my favorite stories so that's an element I wanted to preserve because it's there in the source material. Andy wanted to preserve it and really make that a part of ''It'' because I think those moments of levity provide a great contrast to those darker moments, or makes the darker moments feel all that much darker.\"<ref name=Dauberman/> Dauberman also spoke of the inspiration Muschietti had upon him, as well as director [[James Wan]], while stating that: \"a lot of 80s horror movies and such helped to bring that sort of aesthetic and sensibility.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nightmarishconjurings.com/interviews/2017/9/6/interview-co-writer-gary-dauberman-for-it|title=Interview: Co-Writer Gary Dauberman for IT|last=McGrew|first=Shannon|work=Nightmarish Conjurings|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref>\n\n==Music==\n{{main|It (soundtrack)}}\nOn March 23, 2017, [[Benjamin Wallfisch]] was announced as the composer of ''It''{{'}}s score.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://filmmusicreporter.com/2017/03/23/benjamin-wallfisch-to-score-andres-muschiettis-it/|title=Benjamin Wallfisch to Score Andr\u00e9s Muschietti's 'It' |authors=Film Music Reporter Editors |work=Film Music Reporter|date=March 23, 2017|access-date=April 5, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://joblo.com/horror-movies/news/stephen-king-s-it-will-be-scored-by-lights-out-composer-benjamin-wallfisch-157|title=STEPHEN KING'S IT SCORES LIGHTS OUT COMPOSER BENJAMIN WALLFISCH|last=Sprague|first=Mike|work=[[JoBlo.com]]|date=March 28, 2017|access-date=April 5, 2019}}</ref> Wallfisch stated that [[Jerry Goldsmith]], [[John Williams]], [[Alan Silvestri]], as well as [[Dave Grusin]]'s composition for ''[[The Goonies]]'' (1985) were largely influential in the score of ''It'',<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.reddit.com/r/movies/comments/6zoelw/hi_im_bejamin_wallfisch_film_composer_for_the_new/|title=Hi, I'm Bejamin Wallfisch \u2013 Film composer for the new movie 'IT' - AMA!|website=[[Reddit]]|last=Wallfisch|first=Benjamin|date=September 12, 2017|access-date=June 21, 2018}}</ref> as he felt so passionate about those \"big thematic style of scoring\", albeit at the same time wishing to go beyond the idea that it would be a purely orchestral and adventurous score.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/benjamin-wallfisch-interview-it-movie/|title='IT' Composer Benjamin Wallfisch on the Score's 80s Inspiration, Pennywise's Theme, 'Dunkirk' and More|website=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|last=Chitwood|first=Adam|date=September 5, 2017|access-date=June 21, 2018}}</ref> According to Wallfisch, he had to develop a theme for Pennywise which included finding and creating music that could infect all the other melodies as there are several themes in the film but the Pennywise score is a very quiet and whispered childlike tune using very high strings.<ref name=Music>{{cite web|url=https://www.showbizjunkies.com/music/it-composer-benjamin-wallfisch-interview/|title='It' Composer Benjamin Wallfisch Exclusive Interview on Composing the Music and Pennywise's Theme|website=Showbiz Junkies|last=Finnerty|first=Kevin|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=October 7, 2017}}</ref> Wallfisch spoke of Pennywise's second theme, inspired by Skarsg\u00e5rd's portrayal,<ref name=Music/> in which he used the old children's song \"[[Oranges and Lemons]]\", which had always disturbed him as a child: \"We knew we wanted some kind of children's song to signify Pennywise's strange and demented inner monologue. I also very subtly use certain melodic fragments from it in other themes, for example the piano music that opens and closes the movie.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://indiewire.com/2017/09/it-composer-benjamin-wallfisch-reddit-interview-ama-1201875835/|title='It' Composer Benjamin Wallfisch on That Creepy Children's Song and How He Made Pennywise 'Omnipresent'|last=Dry|first=Jude|work=[[IndieWire]]|date=September 13, 2017|access-date=June 21, 2018}}</ref>\n\n==Release==\n[[File:Grauman's Chinese Theatre, by Carol Highsmith fixed & straightened.jpg|thumbnail|right|upright|[[Grauman's Chinese Theatre]] in  Hollywood, California hosted the world premiere showing of ''It''.]]\n''It'' [[premiered]] at [[Grauman's Chinese Theatre]], on September 5, 2017 in [[Hollywood, Los Angeles, California|Hollywood]], [[California]],<ref>{{cite web|url=https://1iota.com/Show/664/World-Premiere---It|title=WORLD PREMIERE - IT |authors=1iota Editors |work=1iota|date=August 24, 2017|access-date=August 26, 2017}}</ref> after screening as a preview at [[BFI Southbank]] in [[London, England]] on September 4, 2017,<ref>{{cite Institute Editors |work=[[British Film Institute]]|date=July 19, 2017|access-date=August 11, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite NIGHT: It |authors=Fantasy Filmfest Editors |work=Fantasy Filmfest|date=July 20, 2017|access-date=August 11, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite 21, 2017|access-date=August 11, 2017}}</ref> ''It'' was released in 28 countries, including European nations (such as Russia and Netherlands), Middle Eastern nations (such as Israel and UAE), Latin America/Caribbean nations (such as Brazil and Panama), Australia, and New Zealand on September 7;<ref>{{cite web|url=http://wbpsites.com/it/us/releasedates/|title=WORLDWIDE RELEASE DATES |authors=Warner Bros. Editors |work=[[Warner Bros.]]|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=August 13, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://cultofmonster.com.au/it-1/|title=IT Australian/New Zealand Theatrical Release Date & Trailer Revealed! |authors=Cult of Monster Editors |work=Cult of Monster|date=March 30, 2017|access-date=August 13, 2017}}</ref> 15 countries including the [[United Kingdom]], and additional European, and Asian countries, including [[North America]] on September 8.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://ew.com/article/2016/04/22/stephen-king-it-release-date/|title=Stephen King: It movie release date set|last=Robinson|first=Will|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=April 22, 2016|access-date=August 13, 2017}}</ref> On September 9, the film screened at the [[Deauville American Film Festival]] in [[Deauville, France]], where it opened in the official sidebar section, The Premiers.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.festival-deauville.com/pid57/film-2303/it|title=IT by Andy Muschietti - Deauville American Film Festival |authors=Deauville American Film Festival Editors |work=[[Deauville American Film Festival]]|date=August 24, 2017|access-date=August 26, 2017}}</ref> ''It'' was selected to screen at Down Town Taito International Comedy Film Festival in [[Tokyo, Japan]] on September 17.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.shitacome.jp/2017/program/program_hiho.html|title=\"Movie Hidden Treasure\" presents Movie Hidden Treasures Festival |authors=Down Town Taito Editors |work=Down Town Taito International Comedy Film Festival|date=August 14, 2017|access-date=August 21, 2017}}</ref> The film was selected as the opening-film of the Slash Film Festival in [[Vienna, Austria]] on September 21,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://slashfilmfestival.com/2017/07/it-happens/|title=It happens! Opening in the horticulture|last=F|first=Thomas|work=Slash Film Festival|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=August 14, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://diepresse.com/home/kultur/film/5259338/Remake-von-Es-feiert-beim-SlashFestival-OesterreichPremiere|title=Remake of \"It\" celebrates the premiere at the \"Slash\" Festival |authors=Die Presse Editors |work=[[Die Presse]]|date=April 22, 2016|access-date=August 14, 2017}}</ref> ahead of its final bow in Italy on October 19, and in Japan on November 3, 2017.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.warnerbros.it/scheda-film/genere-horror/it/|title=Warner Bros. Italy - October 19 |authors=Warner Bros. Editors |work=[[Warner Bros.]]|date=August 13, 2017|access-date=August 24, 2017}}</ref> On March 7, 2017, the title of the film was announced by [[Stephen King]] as ''Part 1 \u2013 The Losers\u2019 Club''.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-movie-review-stephen-king/#it-movie-stephen-king-review|title=Stephen King Says the New 'It' Movie Succeeds Beyond Expectations|last=Foutch|first=Haleigh|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=March 12, 2017|access-date=March 13, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170312222910/http://collider.com/it-movie-review-stephen-king/#it-movie-stephen-king-review|archive-date=March 12, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/stephen-king-it-movie-remake-verdict-a7617811.html|title=Stephen King calls It remake a 'wonderful production'|last=Shepherd|first=Jack|work=[[The Independent]]|date=March 12, 2017|access-date=March 13, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170314064243/http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/stephen-king-it-movie-remake-verdict-a7617811.html|archive-date=March 14, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On September 8, ''It'' opened in a total of 615 [[IMAX]] openings globally, of which 389 were in North America.<ref name=\"IMAX\">{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/stephen-king-it-home-again-box-office-1202163667/|title=Stephen King's 'It' Scares Life Into Box Office, Beats 'Deadpool' With $13.5M Record Preview; $90M+ 3-Day Possible|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=June 2, 2016|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://joblo.com/horror-movies/news/stephen-king-s-it-will-be-released-in-imax-644|title=FIRST LOOK AT PENNYWISE'S \"FRIENDLY\" GUISE FROM THE NEW IT REBOOT|last=Sprague|first=Mike|work=[[JoBlo.com]]|date=August 15, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref>\n\nA few days before its release, ''[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]'' reported the film broke [[Fandango (ticket service)|Fandango]]'s pre-sales record to become the top horror pre-seller of all-time, eclipsing ''[[Paranormal Activity 3]]'' (2011), as well as setting the record as the site's top pre-seller among September releases, beating ''[[Sully (2016 film)|Sully]]'' (2016).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/it-stephen-king-movie-box-office-1202548791/|title='It,' Stephen King Adaptation, Is Top Horror Pre-Seller in History|last=Lang|first=Brent|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 7, 2017}}</ref> ''Variety'' also reported that MovieTickets.com stated that ''It'' accounted for 54.4% of all tickets sold through September 6,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://syfy.com/syfywire/stephen-kings-it-is-on-target-to-break-box-office-records-with-monster-opening|title=STEPHEN KING'S IT IS ON TARGET TO BREAK BOX OFFICE RECORDS WITH MONSTER OPENING|last=Pinchefsky|first=Carol|work=[[Syfy]]|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=September 7, 2017|archive-date=January 9, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210109235407/https://www.syfy.com/syfywire/stephen-kings-it-is-on-target-to-break-box-office-records-with-monster-opening|url-status=dead}}</ref> with ''It'' selling 8x as many tickets as ''Annabelle: Creation'' (2017) did through two days prior to opening, 6x ''[[The Conjuring 2]]''{{'}}s  (2016) totals with two days to opening, and 15x that of ''[[The Purge: Election Year]]'' (2016) at the same point in the sales cycle.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://pro.boxoffice.com/movietickets-com-advance-ticket-sales-stats/|title=MovieTickets.com: 'IT' Advance Ticket Sales Significantly Ahead of Comparable Horror Releases |authors=BoxOffice Editors |work=[[BoxOffice (magazine)|BoxOffice]]|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref>
