2017|access-date=August 29, 2017}}</ref>\n\n==Reception==\n=== Box office ===\n''It'' grossed $328.8&nbsp;million in the United States and Canada, and $373&nbsp;million in other territories, for a worldwide total of $701.8&nbsp;million, against a production budget of $35\u201340&nbsp;million.<ref name=\"MendelsonForbes\" /><ref name=Office/> The $123.4&nbsp;million earned worldwide in its opening weekend was the [[List of highest-grossing openings for films#Biggest worldwide openings since 2002|29th-largest of all time]] in the United States and Canada.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://boxofficemojo.com/alltime/weekends/|title=OPENING WEEKENDS |authors=Box Office Mojo Editors |work=[[Box Office Mojo]]|date=September 5, 2017|access-date=February 21, 2018}}</ref> ''[[Deadline Hollywood]]'' calculated the net profit of the film to be $293.7&nbsp;million, accounting for production budgets, P&A, talent participation and other costs, against box office grosses and ancillary revenues from home media, placing it fifth on their list of 2017's \"Most Valuable Blockbusters\".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2018/03/it-stephen-king-box-office-movie-profits-1202351455/|title=No. 5 'It' Box Office Profits \u2013 2017 Most Valuable Blockbuster Tournament|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|work=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=March 23, 2018|access-date=April 13, 2018}}</ref>\n\n==== Theatrical run ====\nWith ''It'' playing in 4,103 theaters, it set the record for most venues for an R-rated film, surpassing ''[[Logan (film)|Logan]]''{{'}}s (2017) 4,071 theaters,<ref name=\"Mojo\">{{cite web|url=https://boxofficemojo.com/news/?id=4322&p=.htm|title=Adaptation of Stephen King's 'It' Targets Fall Opening Weekend Record|last=Brevet|first=Brad|work=[[Box Office Mojo]]|date=September 5, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> as well as the record for the largest opening for an R-rated horror movie, improving on ''[[Alien: Covenant]]''{{'}}s (2017) 3,761 theaters.<ref name=Mojo/> The film made $13.5&nbsp;million from Thursday night previews, setting the record for highest amount for an R-rated film, (besting ''[[Deadpool (film)|Deadpool]]''{{'}}s (2016) $12.6&nbsp;million), an R-rated horror film (besting ''Paranormal Activity 3''{{'}}s $8&nbsp;million), a September release,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/08/box-office-it-nets-record-crushing-13-5-million-thursday/#110f16ff4470|title=Box Office: 'It' Breaks Several Records With A Huge $13.5M Thursday|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 8, 2016|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/weekend-box-office-it-movie-scares-up-record-thursday-night-1036714|title=Weekend Box Office: 'It' Scares Up Record $13.5M Thursday Night|last=McClintock|first=Pamela|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=September 8, 2016|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://uk.ign.com/articles/2017/09/08/stephen-kings-it-scores-huge-opening-night|title=STEPHEN KING'S IT SCORES HUGE OPENING NIGHT|last=Gilyadov|first=Alex|work=[[IGN]]|date=September 8, 2016|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> as well as the biggest Thursday preview for any of King's adaptations.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://thewrap.com/it-pennywise-box-office-13-5-million-thursday-record-horror/|title='It' Sets Thursday Box Office Record With Monster $13.5 Million|last=Pressberg|first=Matt|work=[[TheWrap]]|date=September 8, 2016|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> The film opened to $51&nbsp;million on its first day,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/robcain/2017/09/09/with-its-49m-start-stephen-kings-it-is-an-old-fashioned-monster-hit/#75034a9c6fdb|title=With Its $51M Open, Stephen King's 'It' Is An Old-Fashioned Monster Hit|last=Cain|first=Rob|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 9, 2016|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> breaking previous records for the highest-opening R-rated, non-sequel horror film (besting ''[[The Conjuring]]''{{'}}s (2013) $41&nbsp;million), and the highest-opening Stephen King movie (besting ''[[1408 (film)|1408]]''{{'}}s (2007) $20&nbsp;million).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2017/09/it-box-office-records-deadpool-100-million|title=It Devoured Deadpool's Opening Day Record for an R-Rated Movie|last=Stefansky|first=Emma|work=[[Vanity Fair (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]|date=September 9, 2016|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> The $51&nbsp;million also gave ''It'' the biggest single-day opening for an R-rated movie of all time, dethroning ''Deadpool''{{'}}s $46&nbsp;million,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/09/box-office-it-floats-to-record-crushing-51m-friday/#264f98b3481a|title=Box Office: 'It' Floats To Record-Crushing $51M Friday|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 9, 2016|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref> while nearly eclipsing ''Paranormal Activity 3''{{'}}s entire weekend gross of $52.6&nbsp;million, which was the highest opening weekend gross for an R-rated horror film.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/it-box-office-stephen-king-opening-preview-1202549186/|title=Stephen King's 'It' to Jolt Box Office With Monster Opening|last=Kelley|first=Seth|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> Muschietti's ''It'' went on to open to $124&nbsp;million,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/robcain/2017/09/11/stephen-kings-it-balloons-to-124-million-debut-weekend/#2c1439c83883|title=Stephen King's 'It' Balloons To $124 Million Debut Weekend|last=Cain|first=Rob|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 11, 2016|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> setting the records for [[List of highest-grossing openings for films#Biggest opening weekends in the U.S. and Canada|largest opening weekend]] for both a September and a fall release (besting ''[[Hotel Transylvania 2]]''{{'}}s (2015) $48.4&nbsp;million) and (besting ''[[Gravity (2013 film)|Gravity]]''{{'}}s (2013) $55&nbsp;million),<ref name=\"Forbes\">{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/10/six-ways-stephen-kings-it-has-already-made-box-office-history/|title='It' Box Office: 6 Ways The Stephen King Movie's $117M Weekend Made History|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 10, 2017|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> while eclipsing the biggest adjusted September opening (besting ''[[Rush Hour (1998 film)|Rush Hour]]''{{'}}s (1998) $62&nbsp;million) and the biggest adjusted October opening (besting ''[[Scary Movie 3]]''{{'}}s (2003) $71&nbsp;million).<ref name=Forbes/>\n\nOther records set by the film include the largest opening weekend for an R-rated horror film (besting ''Paranormal Activity 3''{{'}}s (2011) $52.6&nbsp;million),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/it-box-office-stephen-king-movie-opening-weekend-1202553361/|title=Box Office: Stephen King's 'It' Smashes Records With Massive $117 Million Opening|last=Kelley|first=Seth|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=September 10, 2017|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> the biggest theatrical debut in horror movie history (besting ''[[Hannibal (2001 film)|Hannibal]]''{{'}}s (2001) $58&nbsp;million),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://thewrap.com/it-box-office-123-million-opening/|title='It' Smashes Box Office Records With $117 Million Opening|last=Fuster|first=Jeremy|work=[[TheWrap]]|date=September 10, 2017|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> the biggest non-holiday/long weekend R-rated debut of all time (besting ''Logan''{{'}}s $88&nbsp;million),<ref name=Forbes/> the cheapest movie ever to top $100&nbsp;million in its debut weekend (besting ''[[The Twilight Saga: New Moon]]''{{'}}s (2009) $50m budget),<ref name=Forbes/> becoming the second-biggest debut for an R-rated film behind ''Deadpool''{{'}}s ($132.4&nbsp;million), the biggest opening for an R-rated movie based upon a book (besting ''[[Fifty Shades of Grey (film)|Fifty Shades of Grey]]''{{'}}s (2015) $85&nbsp;million),<ref name=Forbes/> and the third-highest opening of 2017 (behind ''[[Beauty and the Beast (2017 film)|Beauty and the Beast]]'' and ''[[Guardians of the Galaxy Vol. 2]]''), while joining ''[[The Passion of the Christ]]'' (2004) as the only film under $40&nbsp;million to enter the biggest openers list.<ref name=Forbes/> ''[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]'' noted that the film's opening weekend could have been even greater if not for [[Hurricane Irma]] shutting down nearly 50% of Florida's theaters, a state that typically accounts for 5% of the country's box office grosses.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/hurricane-irma-theater-closures-it-movie-1202553537/|title=Hurricane Irma Causes More Movie Theater Closures as Storm Makes Second Landfall|last=Khatchatourian|first=Maane|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=September 10, 2017|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> The film broke the record for the highest Monday that the month of September has ever seen with $8.8&nbsp;million (besting ''[[The Sixth Sense]]''{{'}}s (1999) $6.37&nbsp;million),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/it-movie-stephen-king-september-record-monday-1202167805/|title='It' Posts Record Monday For September With $8.8M|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 12, 2017|access-date=September 13, 2017}}</ref> the biggest Monday ever for an R-rated horror and/or scary movie,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/12/it-box-office-pennywise-dances-past-200-million-worldwide|title='It' Box Office: Pennywise Dances Past $200 Million Worldwide|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 12, 2017|access-date=September 21, 2017}}</ref> while breaking the record  for the highest Tuesday that the month of September has ever seen with $11.4&nbsp;million (besting ''Sully''{{'}}s $4.8&nbsp;million),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/it-movie-stephen-king-tuesday-box-office-record-september-october-box-office-1202168696/|title='It' Scares Up $11.4M, Biggest Tuesday Ever For September; Stephen King Film To Clear $200M This Weekend|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 13, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> the highest Tuesday for a horror film (besting ''The Conjuring''{{'}}s $5.6&nbsp;million),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/13/box-office-it-soars-31-for-11-4m-tuesday-143m-five-day-total/#587386d7c526|title=Box Office: 'It' Soars 31% For $11.4M Tuesday And Boffo $144M Cume|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 13, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> and the second-biggest single Tuesday for an R-rated horror film (behind ''[[The Omen (2006 film)|The Omen]]''{{'}}s (2006) $12.6&nbsp;million).<ref name=\"Wednesday\">{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/14/it-didnt-need-overseas-box-office-to-be-a-monster-hit/#7fea6bde539c|title=Stephen King's 'It' Didn't Need China To Be A Box Office Monster|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 14, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> The film went on to bring in $7.9&nbsp;million to attain the biggest Wednesday in September history and the biggest Wednesday for an R-rated horror movie,<ref name=Wednesday/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://movieweb.com/it-movie-box-office-records-every-day/|title=IT Has Set a New Box Office Record Every Day Since Release|last=Scott|first=Ryan|work=[[MovieWeb]]|date=September 16, 2017|access-date=September 21, 2017}}</ref> while becoming the record holder for any horror film on a Thursday in September with $7.2&nbsp;million.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://thewrap.com/it-box-office-record/|title='It' Has Broken a Box Office Record Every Day for Past Week|last=Fuster|first=Jeremy|work=[[TheWrap]]|date=September 15, 2017|access-date=September 21, 2017}}</ref>\n\nThe film became the highest-grossing Stephen King horror film ever in North America and worldwide, even adjusted for inflation (besting ''[[The Shining (film)|The Shining]]''{{'}}s (1980) $145&nbsp;million).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/15/box-office-it-is-already-the-biggest-stephen-king-horror-hit-ever/#e41de272cc42|title=Box Office: 'It' Is Stephen King's Biggest Horror Hit Ever|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 15, 2017|access-date=September 21, 2017}}</ref> ''It'' went on to open to $60&nbsp;million, setting the records for the largest second opening weekend for a September release, while also pushing the domestic total to $218.7&nbsp;million to become the highest-grossing September film of all time (besting ''[[Crocodile Dundee]]''{{'}}s (1984) $174.8&nbsp;million).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/it-stephen-king-movie-jennifer-lawrence-mother-dylan-obrien-american-assassin-weekend-box-office-1202170367/|title='It' Becomes Biggest-Ever September Release With $218.8M As 'Mother!' Gets F Report Card & Dismal $7.5M \u2013 Monday Final|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 18, 2017|access-date=September 20, 2017}}</ref> The film went on to become the highest-grossing film ever between the Labor Day-to-November frame.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/it-biggest-horror-pic-ever-domestic-box-office-annabelle-creation-100-million-1202173653/|title='It' Becoming Biggest Horror Pic Ever Beating 'The Exorcist'; 'Annabelle: Creation' Scares Up $100M+|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 20, 2017|access-date=September 25, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/21/stephen-kings-it-is-about-to-break-a-44-year-old-box-office-record|title=Box Office: 'It' Passing 'The Exorcist' To Become Highest-Grossing R-Rated Scary Movie Ever|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 21, 2017|access-date=September 25, 2017}}</ref> Muschietti's ''It'' went on to earn to $236.3&nbsp;million domestic, setting the records for highest-grossing horror film of all time in unadjusted domestic gross (besting ''[[The Exorcist (film)|The Exorcist]]''{{'}}s (1973) $232.9&nbsp;million),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/it-stephen-king-highest-grossing-horror-film-1202566209/|title=Box Office: 'It' Becomes Highest-Grossing Horror Film of All Time|last=Lang|first=Brent|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=September 22, 2016|access-date=September 22, 2017}}</ref> the highest-grossing horror in unadjusted worldwide gross (besting ''The Exorcist''{{'}}s $441&nbsp;million),<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/24/box-office-it-has-scared-up-a-record-crushing-478m-worldwide|title=Box Office: 'It' Has Scared Up A Record-Crushing $478M Worldwide|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 24, 2016|access-date=September 25, 2017}}</ref> while becoming the biggest Stephen King adaptation ever in North America for adjusted gross (besting ''[[The Green Mile (film)|The Green Mile]]''{{'}}s (1999) $233&nbsp;million).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/22/it-celebrated-stephen-kings-birthday-by-breaking-a-few-box-office-records|title=Box Office: 'It' Is Now The Highest-Grossing R-Rated Horror Movie Ever|last=Mendelson|first=Scott|work=[[Forbes]]|date=September 22, 2016|access-date=September 22, 2017}}</ref> In its third weekend, ''It'' was dethroned by newcomer ''[[Kingsman: The Golden Circle]]'', finishing second at the box office with $30&nbsp;million.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/kingsman-the-golden-circle-friend-request-lego-ninjago-box-office-weekend-1202174929/|title='Kingsman: The Golden Circle' Ropes $39M; 'Ninjago' Dulls Sword To $21M+; 'Friend Request' A Loner With $2M+|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 24, 2017|access-date=September 25, 2017}}</ref> On September 28, it passed the $500&nbsp;million mark becoming the 176th film to do so, while becoming second-biggest movie ever starring a clown behind ''[[The Dark Knight (film)|The Dark Knight]]'' (2008).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/scottmendelson/2017/09/28/box-office-stephen-kings-it-floats-past-500-million-worldwide/#6a40c65f529a|title=Box Office: Stephen King's 'It' Floats Past $500 projected gross of $17.3&nbsp;million, apparently retaking its top spot at the box office ahead of ''Kingsman: The Golden Circle'' ($17&nbsp;million).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/kingsman-the-golden-circle-box-office-beats-american-made-it-1202578691/|title=Box Office: 'Kingsman 2' Narrowly Wins Weekend Over 'American Made,' $16.90&nbsp;million to ''Kingsman''{{'}}s $16.93&nbsp;million, while beating out newcomer ''[[American Made (film)|American Made]]'' (2017) ($16.8&nbsp;million).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/10/tom-cruise-emma-stone-american-made-battle-of-the-sexes-flatliners-weekend-box-office-1202179279/|title='Kingsman' Edges Out 'It' In Fierce Three-Way B.O. continued to hold well in the following weeks, making $10&nbsp;million and $6.1&nbsp;million in its fifth and sixth weeks, finishing a respective third and fourth at the box office.<ref>{{cite $26M+ Opening|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=October 15, 2017|access-date=October 17, 2017}}</ref>\n\n==== International run ====\nInternationally, the film was released on approximately 10,560 screens.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/weekend-box-office-it-movie-scares-up-record-thursday-night-1036714|title=Weekend Box Office: opened in 46 markets, breaking opening first day records in various key countries.<ref name=\"September\">{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/it-movie-stephen-king-overseas-62-million-opening-spider-man-800-million-world-wide-international-box-office-1202166067/|title='It' Breaks Genre Records With $62M ($4.6&nbsp;million), Brazil ($1.9&nbsp;million), Russia ($1.3&nbsp;million), Australia ($1.1&nbsp;million), Spain ($1&nbsp;million), Holland ($270,000) and in 5 other countries across Eastern Europe.<ref name=\"International\">{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/stephen-king-it-movie-records-international-box-office-results-1202165333/|title=Stephen King's 'It' Popping Records As generated large opening days were South Korea ($554,000), and the United Arab Emirates ($360,000).<ref name=International/> IMAX generated $10&nbsp;million globally which makes it Warner Bros.' best ever worldwide September play, while also becoming IMAX's best opening in any September in history.<ref name=September/>\n\nAfter the nine days, ''It'' had a total gross of $152.6&nbsp;million from 10,560 screens in 56 markets, while dominating Mexico ($13.85&nbsp;million) on 4,300 screens, while breaking various records in the market.<ref>{{cite ($14.9&nbsp;million) and Brazil ($14.5&nbsp;million), with new record breaking opening in France ($6.3&nbsp;million) and Argentina ($4.1&nbsp;million).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/kingsman-the-golden-circle-lego-ninjago-it-movie-spider-man-homecoming-war-for-the-planet-of-the-apes-weekend-results-international-box-office-1202175753/|title='Kingsman: The film's largest markets were the United Kingdom ($42.5&nbsp;million), Germany ($35.4&nbsp;million), Mexico ($27.6&nbsp;million), France ($20.2&nbsp;million) and Japan ($19.2&nbsp;million).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2018/01/it-crosses-700-million-worldwide-box-office-1202241882/|title='It' Balloons To $700M+ At Worldwide Box Opening|last=Fuster|first=Jeremy|work=[[TheWrap]]|date=August 24, 2017|access-date=September 4, 2017}}</ref> a figure that would give ''It'' the biggest theatrical debut in horror movie history, surpassing ''[[Hannibal (2001 film)|Hannibal]]''{{'}}s (2001) $58&nbsp;million,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://uk.movies.yahoo.com/expected-biggest-opening-weekend-ever-r-rated-horror-162358204.html|title=It expected to have biggest opening weekend ever for an R-rated horror|last=Bussey|first=Ben|work=[[Yahoo! Movies]]|date=August 18, 2017|access-date=September 4, 2017}}</ref> as well as the biggest opening for any film released in September, surpassing ''Hotel Transylvania 2''{{'}}s (2015) $48.4&nbsp;million.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2015/09/the-intern-hotel-transylvania-2-the-green-inferno-weekend-box-office-1201550112/|title='Hotel Transylvania 2' At $48.5M Marks Record Opening For Adam Sandler; 'Intern' Slacks On Sunday \u2013 Monday Postmortem|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 28, 2015|access-date=September 4, 2017}}</ref> Brandon Katz of ''[[The Observer]]'' stated that if ''It'' lives up to its $60&nbsp;million prediction, it could be looking at a worldwide total somewhere around $450&nbsp;million.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://observer.com/2017/08/it-movie-box-officepredictions-tracking-60-million-opening-details/|title=It Looks Like 'It' Is Going to Save 2017's Box Office With Record-Breaking Take|last=Katz|first=Brandon|work=[[The Observer]]|date=August 25, 2017|access-date=September 4, 2017}}</ref> In August, co-editor-in-chief of ''Deadline.com'' Michael Fleming suggested that the film could exceed a $70&nbsp;million opening weekend, and even hit $80&nbsp;million at the box office.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/08/it-movie-andy-muschietti-barbara-muschietti-stephen-king-remake-interview-1202159135/|title=How The Muschietti Siblings Turned Stephen King's Killer Clown Into The 'It' Movie Of Fall \u2013 Q&A|last=Fleming|first=Mike Jr.|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=August 31, 2017|access-date=September 4, 2017}}</ref> C.S. Strowbridge of ''[[The Numbers (website)|The Numbers]]'' estimated that the film would be a box office success, suggesting Muschietti's film to be the biggest hit of the month and dominating the box office in its respective weekend of release.<ref name=\"Numbers\">{{cite web|url=https://the-numbers.com/news/224660830-2017-Preview-September|title=2017 Preview: September|last=Strowbridge|first=C.S.|work=[[The Numbers (website)|The Numbers]]|date=September 1, 2017|access-date=September 4, 2017}}</ref> Strowbridge stated that if the buzz of reception increases then a $60&nbsp;million opening weekend and $160&nbsp;million total becomes more likely, with Strowbridge remarking that ''It'' may even become the all-time highest-grossing film released in September, a record currently held by ''[[Crocodile Dundee]]'' (1986).<ref name=Numbers/> Strowbridge remarked that ''[[Annabelle: Creation]]'' may lose over 1,000 theaters the day ''It'' comes out.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://the-numbers.com/news/224700830-Friday-Estimates-Hitman-Guards-the-Box-Office-with-2-43-million|title=Friday Estimates: Hitman Guards the Box Office with $2.43 million|last=Strowbridge|first=C.S.|work=[[The Numbers (website)|The Numbers]]|date=September 2, 2017|access-date=September 4, 2017}}</ref> By the week of its release, estimates were raised to $60\u201370&nbsp;million in domestic ticket sales.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/09/it-stephen-king-movie-weekend-box-office-1202161829/|title='Box Office To Wake Up From Long Summer's Nap As 'It' Happens With $60Ms Opening, Possible $70M \u2013 Preview|last=D'Alessandro|first=Anthony|website=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 5, 2017|access-date=September 5, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/03/movies/hollywood-summer-box-office-movie-ticket-sales.html|title=After Dismal Summer, Hollywood Pins Hopes on Fall Ticket Sales|last=Barnes|first=Brooks|work=[[The New York Times]]|date=September 3, 2017|access-date=September 5, 2017}}</ref>\n\nBox office analyst Gitesh Pandya spoke of ''It''{{'}}s firepower in which it had earned very good reviews from film critics, as well as the taking-into-account of the historical lucrativeness for horror movies during the October period, with Pandya suggesting a $62&nbsp;million opening weekend.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.boxofficeguru.com/weekend.htm|title=Weekend Box Office (September 8 - 10, 2017)|last=Pandya|first=Gitesh|work=Box Office Guru|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> On September 5, Brad Brevet of ''[[Box Office Mojo]]'' stated that ''It'' film had arrived at the right time, whilst arriving on the heels of the two worst weekends of the year thus far. He also stated that he's forecasting an $85&nbsp;million opening for ''It'', with anything higher not being a surprise.\"<ref name=Mojo/> ''[[The Hollywood Reporter]]'' reported that [[Warner Bros.]]' insiders are being more cautious by stating the figure $60-$65 million, noting the sluggish marketplace, the fact that September has never been known for huge openings, as well as ''It''{{'}}s R rating.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/tracking-record-50m-debut-us-1030473|title='It' Tracking for Record $50M Debut in U.S.|last=McClintock|first=Pamela|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=August 17, 2017|access-date=September 4, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/box-office-preview-stephen-kings-scare-up-record-september-opening-1036122|title=Box-Office Preview: Stephen King's 'It' to Scare Up Record September Opening|last=McClintock|first=Pamela|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> Anita Busch and Anthony D'Alessandro of ''Deadline.com'' reported that Muschietti's ''It'' could run past $90 million, with some trackers looking at $100 million in the film's opening weekend.<ref name=IMAX/>\n\n===Critical response===\n[[File:Bill Skarsgard by Gage Skidmore.jpg|right|thumb|Critics particularly praised [[Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd]]'s portrayal of Pennywise.]]\n''It'' received praise for its performances, direction, screenplay, cinematography, and musical score.<ref>Critical reception for performances, direction, screenplay, cinematography, and its musical score:\n* {{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/it-stephen-king-movie-review-roundup-1202549102/|title=Stephen King's 'It' Reviews: What the Critics Are Saying|last=Nyren|first=Erin|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}\n* {{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/it-review-roundup-1035698|title='It': What the Critics Are Saying|last=Rahman|first=Abid|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}\n* {{cite magazine|url=https://ew.com/movies/2017/09/06/stephen-king-it-movie-reviews/|title=Stephen King's It: The reviews are |last=Rosen|first=Christopher|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}\n* {{cite web|url=https://editorial.rottentomatoes.com/article/it-reviews-see-what-critics-are-saying-about-the-new-stephen-king-adaptation/|title=IT REVIEWS: SEE WHAT CRITICS ARE SAYING ABOUT THE NEW STEPHEN KING ADAPTATION |authors=Rotten Tomatoes Editors |work=[[Rotten Tomatoes]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> On review aggregator [[Rotten Tomatoes]], the film holds an approval rating of 86% based on 388 reviews, with an average rating of 7.30/10. The site's critical consensus reads, \"Well-acted and fiendishly frightening with an emotionally affecting story at its core, ''It'' amplifies the horror in Stephen King's classic story without losing touch with its heart.\"<ref>{{cite Rotten Tomatoes|id=it_2017|type=m|title=It (2017)|access-date=April 4, 2022}}</ref> [[Metacritic]], another [[review aggregator]], assigned the film a weighted average score of 69 out of 100, based on 49 critics, indicating \"generally favorable reviews\".<ref>{{cite Metacritic|id=it|type=movie|title=It (2017)|access-date=March 1, 2021}}</ref> Audiences polled by [[CinemaScore]] gave the film an average grade of \"B+\" on an A+ to F scale, while those at [[PostTrak]] gave it an overall positive score of 85% and a 64% \"definite recommend.\"<ref>{{cite news |last=D'Alessandro |first=Anthony |title='It: Chapter Two' Thursday Night Previews Pop $10.5M \u2013 2nd Friday AM Update|url=https://deadline.com/2019/09/it-chapter-two-opening-weekend-box-office-birds-of-prey-teaser-1202713529/ |access-date=September 6, 2019|work=[[Deadline Hollywood]]|date=September 6, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://thewrap.com/it-box-office-opening-record/|title='It' Stalks $103 Million Opening as Box Office Gets Frightful Boost Despite Irma|last=Fuster|first=Jeremy|work=[[TheWrap]]|date=September 9, 2017|access-date=September 10, 2017}}</ref>\n\n''[[Vanity Fair (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]'',<ref>{{cite (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]|date=November 17, 2017|access-date=November 26, 2017}}</ref> ''[[Salon (website)|Salon]]'',<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.salon.com/2017/09/11/it-deserves-an-array-of-oscars/|title=\"It\" deserves an array of Oscars|last=Rozsa|first=Matthew|work=[[Salon (website)|Salon]]|date=September 11, 2017|access-date=November 26, 2017}}</ref> and ''[[IndieWire]]'',<ref>{{cite web|url=https://indiewire.com/2017/09/it-oscars-stephen-king-best-hairstyle-makeup-1201875127/|title='It' and the Oscars: The One Shot the Horror Blockbuster Has at Becoming a Nominee|last=Sharf|first=Zack|work=[[IndieWire]]|date=September 11, 2017|access-date=November 26, 2017}}</ref> among others, pegged it as an Oscar contender.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.popbuzz.com/tv-film/features/it-oscar-nominations-2018-submission-consideration/#8j7HeRSbFEIjAiIg.97|title=The 'IT' Cast Just Got Submitted For The Oscars...But Will They Win?|last=Wilson-Taylor|first=James|work=PopBuzz|date=November 6, 2017|access-date=November 26, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://joblo.com/horror-movies/news/warner-bros-want-it-considered-for-ocars-including-best-picture-141|title=WARNER BROS WANTS IT CONSIDERED FOR TOP OSCARS INCLUDING BEST PICTURE|last=Sprague|first=Mike|work=[[JoBlo.com]]|date=November 3, 2017|access-date=November 26, 2017}}</ref> Sinead Brennan of ''[[RT\u00c9]]'', awarding four out of five stars, described ''It'' as a \"film that is just beautiful to look at, while you sit on the edge of your seat waiting for the next scare.\"<ref name=\"Brennan\">{{cite web|url=https://www.rte.ie/entertainment/reviews/2017/0831/901290-it/|title=IT delivers scares galore|last=Brennan|first=Sinead|work=[[Raidi\u00f3 Teilif\u00eds \u00c9ireann]]|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> She praised the performances, cinematography, and production value, whilst speaking of Skarsg\u00e5rd as \"chilling perfection\", whose \"manic energy and presence which brings a level of unease and intensity to proceedings that is just incredible.\",<ref name=Brennan/> with Brennan feeling Skarsg\u00e5rd's performance was \"career defining\", and deserving to be considered for awards season.<ref name=Brennan/>\n\nBen Child of ''[[The Guardian]]'' described Skarsg\u00e5rd as a \"revelation\", while stating: \"There may be something of [[Heath Ledger]]'s [[The Joker (The Dark Knight)|Joker]], and a Depression-era New Yoik gangsterism to Skarsg\u00e5rd's vowels, but his ability to go from quiet, leering menace to nightmarish attack mode in a split second is a big part of the appeal.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/film/2017/sep/08/now-youve-seen-it-pennywise-stranger-things-stephen-king|title=Stephen King horror It: Pennywise, the Losers and Stranger Things \u2013 discuss with spoilers|last=Child|first=Ben|work=[[The Guardian]]|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> [[Richard Roeper]] of ''[[The Chicago Sun-Times]]'' spoke most highly of Skarsg\u00e5rd's performance, with him writing \"Skarsg\u00e5rd's Pennywise shows up only sparingly, and that's a wise choice. To be sure, it's a strong performance, and the clown is a worthy successor to all the great scary clowns in movie history\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://chicago.suntimes.com/entertainment/no-doubt-about-it-stephen-king-clown-puts-serious-scares-on-screen/|title=No doubt about 'IT': Stephen King clown puts serious scares on screen|last=Roeper|first=Richard|work=[[The Chicago Sun-Times]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> [[Peter Travers]] of ''[[Rolling Stone]]'' wrote: \"That evil clown Pennywise, a spectacularly scary Bill Skarsg\u00e5rd, is the stuff of nightmares.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.rollingstone.com/movies/reviews/peter-travers-it-will-give-you-killer-clown-nightmares-w501070|title='It' Review: Stephen King's Psycho-Clown Epic 'Is the Stuff of Nightmares'|last=Travers|first=Peter|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> ''[[San Francisco Chronicle]]''\u2019s Peter Hartlaub granted the film a maximum score of four stars, stating that \"Muschietti understands the Spielberg-ian rule, that creating a recognizable and convincing backdrop makes the supernatural thing in the foreground feel tangible and believable.\", while praising Skarsg\u00e5rd and the young cast's performances.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.sfchronicle.com/movies/article/They-got-It-right-Behind-the-horror-and-12177344.php|title=They got 'It' right: Behind the horror and gore lurks real artistry|last=Grierson|first=Tim|work=[[San Francisco Chronicle]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> Ryan Porter of ''[[The Toronto Star]]'' felt Wolfhard to be \"charming in what could have been just another nerd role, proving his breakout performance on ''[[Stranger Things]]'' was more than beginner's luck.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.thestar.com/entertainment/movies/2017/09/07/the-clown-isnt-the-scariest-part-of-it-the-stephen-king-reboot-review.html|title=The clown isn't the scariest part of It, the Stephen King reboot: review|last=Porter|first=Ryan|work=[[The Toronto Star]]|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> In his review for ''[[The St. Louis Post-Dispatch]]'', Calvin Wilson wrote, \"Muschietti conjures an atmosphere of dread that allows for the occasional burst of humor.\" He continued by praising the performances of Muschietti's young cast, citing Lillis whose \"spunky charisma brings to mind [[Scarlett Johansson]] and [[Emma Stone]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.stltoday.com/entertainment/movies/reviews/it-is-among-the-best-scariest-stephen-king-film-adaptations/article_86f72edf-adcd-54d4-91e7-800f5fe50b67.html|title='It' is among the best, scariest Stephen King film adaptations|last=Wilson|first=Calvin|work=[[The St. Louis Post-Dispatch]]|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref>\n\nMaria Sciullo of ''[[The Pittsburgh Post-Gazette]]'' wrote: \"Dylan Grazer and Lillis are standouts among a pretty good bunch of child actors.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.post-gazette.com/ae/movies/2017/09/06/It-film-review-movie-stephen-king-horror/stories/201709080028|title=Movie review: Fear wears a creepy clown face in 'It'|last=Sciullo|first=Maria|work=[[The Pittsburgh Post-Gazette]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> Tasha Robinson of ''[[The Verge]]'' praised all seven of the central children, saying each are \"well-cast and give strong performances\" in the film.<ref name=\"Robinson\">{{cite web|url=https://www.theverge.com/2017/9/6/16257788/it-movie-review-stephen-king-andy-muschietti-pennywise-the-clown|title=Stephen King's It is the rare monster movie with too much monster|last=Robinson|first=Tasha|work=[[The Verge]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> She also said Ray Taylor's portrayal of Ben Hanscom is \"surprisingly tender and nuanced\", Skarsg\u00e5rd seemed \"like a real threat\" as Pennywise, and that Lillis is close to \"heartbreaking\" as Beverly Marsh.<ref name=Robinson/> Christy Lemire of ''[[RogerEbert.com]]'' wrote that \"Despite the many terrifying moments they endure in their quest scenes that will leave you trembling and giggling at once It is even more powerful in the warm, easy camaraderie between its young stars.\"<ref name=\"Lemire\">{{cite web|url=https://rogerebert.com/reviews/it-2017|title=It|last=Lemire|first=Christy|work=[[RogerEbert.com]]|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> Lemire praised the \"well-chosen\" cast, saying the \"that combination of tones\" from the performances make the film work.<ref name=Lemire/> She spoke of Skarsg\u00e5rd as \"working well,\" as he doesn't appear to be laboring so hard to frighten, and that Lillis displays a \"star-making\" performance\".<ref name=Lemire/> Marc Savlov of ''[[The Austin Chronicle]]'' heralded the film, its director, and screenwriters, by stating: \"Muschietti and screenwriters Palmer, Fukunaga, and Dauberman have managed the translation to the big screen nearly as well as [[Rob Reiner]] did with ''[[Stand by Me (film)|Stand by Me]]'' (1986).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.austinchronicle.com/calendar/film/2017-09-08/it/|title=It|last=Savlov|first=Marc|work=[[The Austin Chronicle]]|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> ''[[Entertainment Weekly]]'' journalist Chris Nashawaty summarized \"''It'' is essentially two movies. The better by far is the one that feels like a darker ''Stand by Me'' (1986) a nostalgic coming-of-age story about seven likable outcasts riding around on their bikes and facing their fears together.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://ew.com/movies/2017/09/06/it-movie-review/|title=It delivers the scares, despite too much clowning around|last=Nashawaty|first=Chris|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017|archive-date=September 7, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170907061147/http://ew.com/movies/2017/09/06/it-movie-review/|url-status=dead}}</ref> Tim Grierson of ''[[Screen International]]'' spoke highly of Claude Par\u00e9 and Chung Chung-hoon's ability to \"drape the horror scenes in a clammy atmosphere\", without seeming too far removed from \"the otherwise realistic portrayal of racism, sexual humiliation and bullying\" of Muschetti's piece.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.screendaily.com/reviews/it-review/5121894.article|title='It': Review|last=Grierson|first=Tim|work=[[Screen International]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> Katie Rife, writing for ''[[The A.V. Club]]'', commended Chung's cinematography as succeeding at \"giving the film a richness and texture that's far beyond that of most Hollywood films, let alone horror films.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://avclub.com/nightmarish-imagery-helps-it-float-above-a-clunky-scrip-1800670625|title=Nightmarish imagery helps It float above a clunky script|last=Rife|first=Katie|work=[[The A.V. Club]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref>\n\nThe film, however, was not without criticism, as some critics were disappointed with the film's implementation of [[jump scare]]s.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://indiewire.com/2017/09/it-review-roundup-stephen-king-disappointment-1201873469/|title='It' Reviews Are Disappointed the Film Uses 'Too Many Jump Scares' That Don't Add Up|last=Sharf|first=Zack|work=[[IndieWire]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> \n[[Michael Phillips (critic)|Michael Phillips]] of ''[[The Chicago Tribune]]'' noted the film's \"diminishing returns of one jump scare after another\", writing that \"nearly every scene begins and ends the same way, with a slow build leading up to a KAAA-WHUMMMMMM!!!! sound effect\".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.chicagotribune.com/entertainment/movies/sc-mov-it-review-0906-story.html|title='It' review: Stand by me, and we'll deal with this clown|last=Phillips|first=Michael|work=[[The Chicago Tribune]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> [[Stephanie Zacharek]] of ''[[Time (magazine)|Time]]'' spoke highly of Muschietti's direction, however, she stated: \"Muschietti relies too much on your garden-variety jump scares and now-standard special effects. As always, the horrors you get a close look at are much less terrifying than those that remain unseen.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://time.com/4934369/movie-review-it-stephen-king/|title=Review: Slick and Entertaining, It Can't Match the Horror of Stephen King's Classic|last=Zacharek|first=Stephanie|magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]|date=September 8, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> Erik Henriksen of ''[[The Stranger (newspaper)|The Stranger]]'' praised the \"phenomenal\" young cast, but regretted that the film felt disappointingly bloodless.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.thestranger.com/film/2017/09/06/25395952/it-heres-that-creepy-clown-you-ordered|title=It: Here's That Creepy Clown You Ordered!|last=Henriksen|first=Erik|work=[[The Stranger (newspaper)|The Stranger]]|date=September 6, 2017|access-date=September 14, 2017}}</ref> Lindsey Bahr of ''[[The Associated Press]]'' criticized the story being an \"unforgivable mess\", with Bahr remarking: \"Instead of building tension and suspense, \u201cIt\u201d just jumps from scene to scares with no connection or coherence to thread them together other than the mere fact that they've been placed on top of one-another, like toys mixed up from different sets.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://apnews.com/05193fd73a904c349a2c1f829fea2223/Review:-A-few-good-scares-can't-hold-'It'-together|title=Review: A few good scares can't hold 'It' Area Film Critics Association Award for Best Ensemble|Best Acting Ensemble]]\n| ''It''\n| {{Nominated}}\n|-\n|}\n\n==Sequel and prequel==\n{{main|It Chapter Two}}\nProducer [[Roy Lee]] mentioned a second planned film in an interview with [[Collider (website)|Collider]] on February 16, 2016, before principal photography had begun on the first film, saying, \"Dauberman wrote the most recent draft working with Muschietti, so it's being envisioned as two movies.\"<ref name=Muschietti>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-movie-news-rating/|title=Exclusive: 'It' Movie Hopefully Shooting This Year; Will Be Rated-R|last=Chitwood|first=Adam|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=February 19, 2016|access-date=June 27, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160626211828/http://collider.com/it-movie-news-rating/|archive-date=June 26, 2016|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On July 19, 2017, Muschietti revealed that the plan is to get production underway for the sequel to ''It'' during the following spring, adding,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-part-2-director-andy-muschietti/|title='IT' Director Andy Muschietti Says He's Coming Back for a Sequel|last=Foutch|first=Haleigh|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=July 19, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170720053246/http://collider.com/it-part-2-director-andy-muschietti/|archive-date=July 20, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://screenrant.com/it-movie-sequel-filming-2018-start/|title=Second IT Movie Adaptation Aims to Start Filming Next Year|last=Zinski|first=Dan|work=[[Screen Rant]]|date=July 19, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170721010304/https://screenrant.com/it-movie-sequel-filming-2018-start/|archive-date=July 21, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> \"We'll probably have a script for the second part in January 2018. Ideally, we would start prep in March. Part one is only about the kids. Part two is about these characters 30 years later as adults, with flashbacks to 1989 when they were kids.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://syfy.com/syfywire/it-already-has-a-sequel-planned|title=Stephen King's It Already has a Sequel Planned|last=Wax|first=Alyse|work=[[Syfy]]|date=July 20, 2017|access-date=July 20, 2017|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170720065345/https://syfy.com/syfywire/it-already-has-a-sequel-planned|archive-date=July 20, 2017|df=mdy-all}}</ref> On July 21, 2017, Muschietti spoke of looking forward to having a dialogue in the second film that does not exist within the first, stating, it seems like we're going to do it. It's the second half, it's not a sequel. It's the second half and it's very connected to the first one.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-movie-andy-muschietti-interview-sdcc/|title='IT' Director Andy Muschietti on Reinventing Pennywise and Sequel Plans|last=Foutch|first=Haleigh|work=[[Collider (website)|Collider]]|date=July 21, 2017|access-date=July 22, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://cinemablend.com/news/1683730/why-the-it-movie-left-the-adult-storyline-out-of-the-first-film|title=Why The IT Movie Left The Adult Storyline Out Of The First Film|last=O'Connell|first=Sean|work=CinemaBlend|date=July 22, 2017|access-date=July 23, 2017}}</ref> Muschietti confirmed that two cut scenes from the film will hopefully be included in the second, one of which being the fire at the Black Spot from the book.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://collider.com/it-movie-cut-scenes|title=The 'IT' Movie Had to Cut Two Crazy Scenes to Stay On-Budget|last=Foutch|first=Haleigh|work=Collider.com|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=July 27, 2017}}</ref>\n\nOn September 25, 2017, [[New Line Cinema]] announced that the sequel would be released on September 6, 2019,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/it-movie-sequel-release-date-1202570309/|title='It' Sequel Sets September 2019 Release Date|last=McNary|first=Dave|work=[[Variety.com]]|date=September 25, 2017|access-date=July 25, 2017}}</ref> with [[Gary Dauberman]] writing the script.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/it-sequel-plans-moving-forward-at-new-line-1035456|title='It' Movie Sequel Plans Move Forward at New Line|last=Kit|first=Borys|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|date=September 7, 2017|access-date=July 25, 2017}}</ref> Later in December 2017, ''[[Agent Cody Banks]]'' writer Jeffrey Jurgensen was also listed as a screenwriter.<ref>{{cite web|last=McNary|first=Dave|url=https://variety.com/2017/film/news/are-you-afraid-of-the-dark-movie-release-1202632308/|title=''Are You Afraid Of The Dark?'' Movie Gets October 2019 Release|date=December 6, 2017|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|access-date=December 6, 2017}}</ref> {{as of|2018|February}}, [[Jessica Chastain]] was in negotiations to star as the adult Beverly Marsh.<ref>{{cite web|last=Schmitz|first=Greg|url=https://editorial.rottentomatoes.com/article/jessica-chastain-to-play-adult-beverly-in-it-chapter-two-and-more-movie-news/|title=''Jessica Chastain to Play Adult Beverly in IT: Chapter Two, and More Movie News''|date=February 23, 2018|website=[[Rotten Tomatoes]]|access-date=February 24, 2018}}</ref> In April 2018, [[James McAvoy]] and [[Bill Hader]] entered negotiations to play the adult Bill Denbrough and Richie Tozier.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2018/film/news/james-mcavoy-and-bill-hader-it-sequel-1202749616/|title=James McAvoy, Bill Hader in Talks for 'It: Chapter 2'|first=Justin|last=Kroll|date=April 12, 2018}}</ref> In May 2018, [[James Ransone]] revealed on Twitter that he would play the adult Eddie Kaspbrak.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://consequenceofsound.net/2018/05/james-ransone-it-chapter-two/|title=James Ransone signs on to play Eddie Kaspbrak in It: Chapter Two|date=May 16, 2018|work=Consequence of Sound|access-date=May 16, 2018}}</ref> Shortly afterwards, [[Andy Bean (actor)|Andy Bean]] and [[Jay Ryan (actor)|Jay Ryan]] had joined the cast to play the adult Stanley Uris and Ben Hanscom respectively.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://variety.com/2018/film/news/andy-bean-stanley-it-chapter-2-exclusive-1202812635/|title='It: Chapter 2' Taps Andy Bean to Play Stanley (EXCLUSIVE)|website=Variety|last=Kroll|first=Justin|date=May 16, 2018|access-date=May 16, 2018}}</ref> In June 2018, [[Isaiah Mustafa]] signed on to play the adult Mike Hanlon.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2018/film/news/it-chapter-2-mike-hanlon-isaiah-mustafa-1202838872/|title='It: Chapter 2' Casts Isaiah Mustafa as Adult Mike|last=Kroll|first=Justin|work=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|date=June 9, 2018|access-date=May 13, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190629082455/https://variety.com/2018/film/news/it-chapter-2-mike-hanlon-isaiah-mustafa-1202838872/|archive-date=June 29, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nFilming had officially begun on June 19, 2018, and concluded in November 2018. Shooting took a total of 86 days.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.instagram.com/p/BkOSl0_HUqv/ |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/iarchive/instagram/jamesmcavoyrealdeal/1805462264973445807_1805462124447435721 |archive-date=2021-12-23 |title=Day 1 on IT 2. 2, 2018|accessdate=June 11, 2021}}</ref> The film was released on September 6, 2019, and was a box office success although it garnered a mixed critical reception.<ref>{{Cite web |last=D'Alessandro Max]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=Otterson |first=Joe |last2=Otterson |first2=Joe |date=2022-11-09 |title=\u2018It\u2019 Prequel Series at HBO Max Taps Jason Fuchs, Brad Caleb Kane to Serve as
